🏗️ Workload Resources

Kubernetes workload resources manage the deployment and execution of your applications. In this section, we'll explore how to deploy and manage your anihpj Django application using various workload resources, starting with ReplicationController - a fundamental resource for maintaining desired replica counts of your Django pods.

📋 Workload Resources Overview

ReplicationController - Ensures desired replica count
Deployment - Declarative updates for apps
StatefulSet - Ordered, persistent apps
DaemonSet - One pod per node
Job - Run-to-completion tasks
CronJob - Scheduled jobs
🎯 Django Focus: This documentation shows practical examples of deploying the anihpj Django project with its jobpost app models (Skills, Author, Location, JobPost) to Kubernetes using real manifests and kubectl commands. The jobpost app provides JSON APIs for job listings, job details, and skills management.

ReplicationController

ReplicationController Overview

ReplicationControllerSpec - Desired state specification
ReplicationControllerStatus - Current observed status
ReplicationControllerCondition - State condition details
ReplicationControllerList - Collection of controllers
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: ReplicationController v1 API | API Version: v1

ReplicationController represents the configuration of a replication controller that ensures a specified number of pod replicas are running at any given time.

Full Description

ReplicationController is one of the oldest workload resources in Kubernetes, designed to ensure that a specified number of identical pods are running at all times. When deploying your anihpj Django application, a ReplicationController will monitor your Django pods and automatically create new ones if any fail or are deleted, ensuring high availability for your jobpost application.

While ReplicationController has largely been superseded by Deployment (which provides additional features like rolling updates), it's still fundamental to understand as it forms the basis for more advanced workload resources. In production Django deployments, you'll typically use Deployments, but ReplicationController is perfect for understanding basic pod replication concepts.

Syntax

# Create a ReplicationController from YAML file
kubectl create -f replicationcontroller.yaml
# List all ReplicationControllers (long form)
kubectl get replicationcontrollers
# List all ReplicationControllers (short form)
kubectl get rc
# Get detailed information about a specific ReplicationController
kubectl describe replicationcontroller {name}
# Get detailed information about a specific ReplicationController (short form)
kubectl describe rc {name}
# Scale ReplicationController to specified number of replicas
kubectl scale replicationcontroller {name} --replicas={count}
# Scale ReplicationController to specified number of replicas (short form)
kubectl scale rc {name} --replicas={count}
# Delete a specific ReplicationController
kubectl delete replicationcontroller {name}
# Delete a specific ReplicationController (short form)
kubectl delete rc {name}

YAML Structure

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-django-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: web
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: web
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-web
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: Always "v1" for ReplicationController. This indicates the API version being used.
  • kind: Must be "ReplicationController" to specify the resource type.
  • metadata.name: Unique name for the ReplicationController within the namespace. Use descriptive names like "anihpj-django-rc".
  • metadata.namespace: Kubernetes namespace where the ReplicationController will be created. Defaults to "default".
  • metadata.labels: Key-value pairs for organizing and selecting ReplicationControllers. Useful for grouping Django app components.
  • spec.replicas: Desired number of pod replicas. For Django apps, start with 2-3 for high availability.
  • spec.selector: Label selector to identify which pods belong to this ReplicationController. Must match template labels.
  • spec.template: Pod template specification that defines how new pods should be created.
  • spec.template.metadata.labels: Labels applied to created pods. Must include selector labels.
  • spec.template.spec: Pod specification including containers, volumes, and other pod-level configurations.
  • spec.minReadySeconds: Minimum seconds a pod must be ready before considered available. Useful for Django apps with startup time.

Return Value

Returns the ReplicationController object with its current state, including status information about replicas, ready replicas, and conditions indicating the controller's health.

  • 200 OK: ReplicationController successfully created/updated
  • 201 Created: ReplicationController successfully created
  • 400 Bad Request: Invalid ReplicationController specification
  • 401 Unauthorized: Authentication required
  • 403 Forbidden: Insufficient permissions
  • 404 Not Found: Namespace not found
  • 409 Conflict: ReplicationController already exists
  • 422 Unprocessable Entity: Invalid field values

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Skills Model Service (jobpost app)

This example demonstrates deploying a ReplicationController for the Skills API service (/jobpost/skills/), providing JSON endpoints for managing available job skills in the anihpj Django project.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: skills
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: skills
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost
        service: skills
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-skills
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_APP
          value: "jobpost"
        - name: MODEL_FOCUS
          value: "skills"
# Apply the Skills model ReplicationController
kubectl apply -f anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc.yaml
replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc created
Example 2: Author Model Service (jobpost app)

This example shows how to deploy author management services using ReplicationController for the Author model, which connects to Django's built-in User model for authentication.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-author-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: author
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: author
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost
        service: author
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-author
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_APP
          value: "jobpost"
        - name: MODEL_FOCUS
          value: "user"
        - name: DB_PATH
          value: "/app/db.sqlite3"
# Create the Author model ReplicationController
kubectl create -f anihpj-jobpost-author-rc.yaml
replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-author-rc created

Example 4: JobPost Model Service (jobpost app)

This example demonstrates deploying the core JobPost model service using ReplicationController for handling job posting operations in the anihpj Django project.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-location-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: location
spec:
  replicas: 1
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: location
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost
        service: location
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-location
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_APP
          value: "jobpost"
        - name: MODEL_FOCUS
          value: "location"
        - name: GEO_API_KEY
          value: "your-maps-api-key"
# Dry run to validate Location model ReplicationController YAML
kubectl create -f anihpj-jobpost-location-rc.yaml --dry-run=client -o yaml
apiVersion: v1 kind: ReplicationController metadata: name: anihpj-jobpost-location-rc namespace: default spec: replicas: 1 selector: app: anihpj component: jobpost service: location
Example 5: JobPost Model Main Service (jobpost app)

This example shows the main JobPost API service deployment (/jobpost/jobs/), handling job listing and detail operations with comprehensive configuration for the anihpj Django project's core functionality.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-main-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: jobpost-main
spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: jobpost-main
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost
        service: jobpost-main
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-main
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: DJANGO_APP
          value: "jobpost"
        - name: MODEL_FOCUS
          value: "jobpost"
        - name: ALLOWED_HOSTS
          value: "jobpost.anihpj.com"
# Apply JobPost main service ReplicationController and list all RCs
kubectl apply -f anihpj-jobpost-main-rc.yaml && kubectl get rc
replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-main-rc created NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY AGE anihpj-jobpost-main-rc 4 4 4 10s
- name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE value: "anihpj.settings"

kubectl commands:

# Create the ReplicationController
kubectl apply -f anihpj-django-rc.yaml

# Check ReplicationController status
kubectl get rc anihpj-django-rc

# View detailed information
kubectl describe rc anihpj-django-rc
NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY AGE anihpj-django-rc 3 3 3 45s ReplicationController: anihpj-django-rc Namespace: default Selector: app=anihpj-django,component=web Labels: app=anihpj-django,component=web Replicas: 3 current / 3 desired Pods Status: 3 Running / 0 Waiting / 0 Succeeded / 0 Failed

Example 3: Django with ConfigMap and Secrets

This example shows how to deploy Django with external configuration using ConfigMaps and Secrets for secure credential management.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-secure-rc
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    tier: production
spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    tier: production
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        tier: production
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-secure
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:secure
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        envFrom:
        - configMapRef:
            name: django-config
        - secretRef:
            name: django-secrets
        volumeMounts:
        - name: static-files
          mountPath: /app/staticfiles
      volumes:
      - name: static-files
        emptyDir: {}

kubectl commands:

# First create ConfigMap and Secret
# Create Django configuration map with allowed hosts
kubectl create configmap django-config --from-literal=ALLOWED_HOSTS="*"
# Create Django secrets for sensitive data
kubectl create secret generic django-secrets --from-literal=SECRET_KEY="your-secret-key"

# Deploy secure Django setup
kubectl apply -f secure-django-rc.yaml

# Monitor deployment
kubectl get rc,pods -l tier=production
configmap/django-config created secret/django-secrets created replicationcontroller/anihpj-secure-rc created NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY AGE replicationcontroller/anihpj-secure-rc 4 4 4 1m32s NAME READY STATUS RESTARTS AGE pod/anihpj-secure-rc-4h7j2 1/1 Running 0 1m32s pod/anihpj-secure-rc-8k5m1 1/1 Running 0 1m32s pod/anihpj-secure-rc-n9p6w 1/1 Running 0 1m32s pod/anihpj-secure-rc-q2x8v 1/1 Running 0 1m32s
Example 4: Django with Health Checks and Resource Limits

This example demonstrates deploying Django with proper health checks, resource constraints, and monitoring capabilities for production environments.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-healthy-rc
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    version: v2
spec:
  replicas: 3
  minReadySeconds: 30
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    version: v2
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        version: v2
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-healthy
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5

kubectl commands:

# Deploy with health checks
kubectl apply -f healthy-django-rc.yaml

# Watch pod readiness
kubectl get pods -l version=v2 -w

# Check resource usage
kubectl top pods -l app=anihpj
replicationcontroller/anihpj-healthy-rc created NAME READY STATUS RESTARTS AGE anihpj-healthy-rc-b8m4k 0/1 Running 0 15s anihpj-healthy-rc-d2n7x 0/1 Running 0 15s anihpj-healthy-rc-f5p9q 0/1 Running 0 15s anihpj-healthy-rc-b8m4k 1/1 Running 0 35s anihpj-healthy-rc-d2n7x 1/1 Running 0 35s anihpj-healthy-rc-f5p9q 1/1 Running 0 35s NAME CPU(cores) MEMORY(bytes) anihpj-healthy-rc-b8m4k 128m 245Mi anihpj-healthy-rc-d2n7x 115m 238Mi anihpj-healthy-rc-f5p9q 142m 251Mi
Example 5: Django Background Task Workers

This example illustrates deploying Django background task workers for processing asynchronous jobs and queue operations.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-worker-rc
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: worker
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: worker
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: worker
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-worker
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:worker
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "process_tasks"]
        env:
        - name: WORKER_TYPE
          value: "jobpost_processor"
        - name: REDIS_URL
          value: "redis://redis-service:6379/0"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"

kubectl commands:

# Deploy background workers
kubectl apply -f worker-rc.yaml

# Check worker logs
kubectl logs -l component=worker --tail=20

# Scale workers based on load
kubectl scale rc anihpj-worker-rc --replicas=6
replicationcontroller/anihpj-worker-rc created Processing JobPost ID: 1 - Python Developer Processing JobPost ID: 2 - Frontend Developer Processing JobPost ID: 3 - Full Stack Developer Processing Skills updates for Author: user1 Processing Location updates for: New York Worker anihpj-worker-rc-k7x3m ready for tasks Worker anihpj-worker-rc-m9p2n ready for tasks replicationcontroller/anihpj-worker-rc scaled

ReplicationControllerSpec

ReplicationControllerSpec defines the desired behavior of the replication controller. For Django applications, carefully consider the replica count based on expected traffic, resource requirements, and high availability needs.

Syntax
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: web
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
  minReadySeconds: 30
Parameters Description
  • selector (map[string]string): Label query over pods that should match the replicas count. If empty, defaults to labels on Pod template. For anihpj Django apps, use labels like app=anihpj, component=web.
  • template (PodTemplateSpec): Defines the pod that will be created if insufficient replicas are detected. Must include restartPolicy: Always for ReplicationController.
  • replicas (int32): Number of desired replicas. For Django production, typically 2-5 replicas for web apps, 1-3 for workers.
  • minReadySeconds (int32): Minimum seconds for a pod to be ready before considered available. Important for Django apps with database connections.
Example 1: Django Web App Spec

This example shows the complete ReplicationController specification for a Django web application with detailed metadata, labels, and container configuration.

spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    tier: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        tier: web
        version: v1.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-web
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
  minReadySeconds: 45
# Apply the Django web specification
kubectl apply -f django-web-spec.yaml
# Get ReplicationController details in wide format
kubectl get rc -o wide
replicationcontroller/anihpj-web-rc configured NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY AGE CONTAINERS IMAGES SELECTOR anihpj-web-rc 4 4 4 2m django-web anihpj/django-web:v1.0 app=anihpj,tier=web
Example 2: JobPost API Service Spec

This example demonstrates a ReplicationController spec for the JobPost API service with database connections and environment-specific settings.

spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    service: jobpost-api
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        service: jobpost-api
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-api
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DB_PATH
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: db-credentials
              key: url
# Create database credentials secret
kubectl create secret generic db-credentials --from-literal=url="sqlite:///db.sqlite3"
# Apply the JobPost API ReplicationController
kubectl apply -f jobpost-api-spec.yaml
secret/db-credentials created replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-api-rc created
Example 3: Skills API Service Spec

This example shows a ReplicationController spec optimized for the Skills API service with specific resource limits and health check configurations.

spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    service: skills-api
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        service: skills-api
        version: v1.2.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: skills-api
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.2.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: API_ENDPOINT
          value: "/jobpost/skills/"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /jobpost/skills/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
  minReadySeconds: 15
# Apply the Skills API ReplicationController specification
kubectl apply -f skills-api-spec.yaml
# Verify the deployment
kubectl get rc anihpj-skills-api-rc -o wide
replicationcontroller/anihpj-skills-api-rc created NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY AGE CONTAINERS IMAGES SELECTOR anihpj-skills-api-rc 3 3 3 45s skills-api anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.2.0 app=anihpj,service=skills-api
Example 4: Author Management Service Spec

This example demonstrates a ReplicationController spec for the Author management service with authentication integration and persistent volume mounts.

spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    service: author-mgmt
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        service: author-mgmt
        tier: backend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: author-service
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: DB_PATH
          value: "/app/data/db.sqlite3"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: sqlite-storage
          mountPath: /app/data
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "150m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"
      volumes:
      - name: sqlite-storage
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-sqlite-pvc
  minReadySeconds: 20
# Create persistent volume claim first
kubectl apply -f sqlite-pvc.yaml
# Apply the Author management service spec
kubectl apply -f author-mgmt-spec.yaml
persistentvolumeclaim/anihpj-sqlite-pvc created replicationcontroller/anihpj-author-mgmt-rc created
Example 5: Location Service with Advanced Configuration

This example shows an advanced ReplicationController spec for the Location service with ConfigMap integration, init containers, and service mesh compatibility.

spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    service: location
    environment: production
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        service: location
        environment: production
        version: v2.0.0
      annotations:
        sidecar.istio.io/inject: "true"
    spec:
      initContainers:
      - name: db-migration
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.0.0
        command: ['python', 'manage.py', 'migrate']
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
      containers:
      - name: location-service
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        - containerPort: 9090
          name: metrics
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        envFrom:
        - configMapRef:
            name: location-config
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "200Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "400Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 10
          periodSeconds: 5
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
  minReadySeconds: 30
# Create location configuration
kubectl create configmap location-config --from-literal=DEBUG=False --from-literal=LOG_LEVEL=INFO
# Apply the advanced location service spec
kubectl apply -f location-advanced-spec.yaml
configmap/location-config created replicationcontroller/anihpj-location-prod-rc created

ReplicationControllerStatus

ReplicationControllerStatus represents the current status of a replication controller, providing visibility into the health and state of your Django application deployment.

Syntax
status:
  replicas: 3
  readyReplicas: 3
  availableReplicas: 3
  fullyLabeledReplicas: 3
  observedGeneration: 1
  conditions:
  - type: ReplicaFailure
    status: "False"
    lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-08T10:30:00Z"
    reason: PodsRunning
    message: "All pods are running successfully"
Parameters Description
  • replicas (int32, required): Most recently observed number of replicas. Monitor this to ensure your Django app maintains desired capacity.
  • availableReplicas (int32): Number of available replicas (ready for at least minReadySeconds). Critical for Django app availability.
  • readyReplicas (int32): Number of ready replicas. Should match desired replicas for healthy Django deployment.
  • fullyLabeledReplicas (int32): Pods with labels matching the pod template labels.
  • conditions ([]ReplicationControllerCondition): Latest observations of the controller's current state.
  • observedGeneration (int64): Generation of the most recently observed replication controller.
Example 1: Healthy Django App Status

This example shows how to check the status of a healthy Django ReplicationController, displaying replica counts and current state.

# Get status section of the Django RC in YAML format
kubectl get rc anihpj-django-rc -o yaml | grep -A 20 "status:"
status: availableReplicas: 3 fullyLabeledReplicas: 3 observedGeneration: 1 readyReplicas: 3 replicas: 3
# Get detailed description of Django RC
kubectl describe rc anihpj-django-rc
Name: anihpj-django-rc Namespace: default Selector: app=anihpj,component=web Labels: app=anihpj,component=web Replicas: 3 current / 3 desired Pods Status: 3 Running / 0 Waiting / 0 Succeeded / 0 Failed Events: Type Reason Age From Message ---- ------ ---- ---- ------- Normal SuccessfulCreate 5m replication-controller Created pod: anihpj-django-rc-abc123

ReplicationControllerCondition

ReplicationControllerCondition describes the state of a replication controller at a certain point in time. This provides detailed insights into why your Django application might be experiencing issues.

Syntax
conditions:
- type: "ReplicaFailure"
  status: "True"
  lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-08T10:30:00Z"
  reason: "FailedCreate"
  message: "Error creating: pods \"anihpj-skills-rc-\" is forbidden"
- type: "Progressing"
  status: "True"
  lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-08T10:25:00Z"
  reason: "NewReplicaSetAvailable"
  message: "ReplicationController has successfully progressed"
Parameters Description
  • type (string, required): Type of replication controller condition. Common types include "ReplicaFailure", "Progressing"
  • status (string, required): Status of the condition, one of "True", "False", "Unknown"
  • lastTransitionTime (Time): The last time the condition transitioned from one status to another
  • reason (string): Machine-readable, UpperCamelCase text indicating the reason for the condition's last transition
  • message (string): Human-readable message indicating details about the transition
Return Value

Conditions are read-only fields populated by the Kubernetes system. They provide status information and are part of the ReplicationController status object.

5 Django Condition Examples
Example 1: Skills Model Healthy Condition (jobpost app)

This example shows how to check the health conditions of the Skills model ReplicationController using formatted JSON output.

# Get conditions of Skills RC in formatted JSON
kubectl get rc anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc -o jsonpath='{.status.conditions}' | python -m json.tool
[ { "lastTransitionTime": "2025-09-08T10:30:00Z", "message": "Skills model ReplicationController has successfully progressed", "reason": "NewReplicaSetAvailable", "status": "True", "type": "Progressing" } ]
Example 2: Author Model Replica Failure (jobpost app)

This example demonstrates how to examine ReplicationController conditions when replica failures occur in the Author model service.

# Get conditions section from User RC description
kubectl describe rc anihpj-jobpost-author-rc | grep -A 5 "Conditions:"
Conditions: Type Status LastTransitionTime Reason ---- ------ ------------------ ------ ReplicaFailure True 2025-09-08T10:35:00Z FailedCreate Progressing False 2025-09-08T10:35:00Z ProgressDeadlineExceeded
Example 3: Author Model Normal Operation (jobpost app)

This example shows how to monitor normal operating conditions of the Author model ReplicationController using kubectl describe.

# Get conditions section of Author RC in YAML format
kubectl get rc anihpj-jobpost-author-rc -o yaml | grep -A 10 "conditions:"
conditions: - lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-08T10:40:00Z" message: "Author model ReplicationController has successfully progressed" reason: "NewReplicaSetAvailable" status: "True" type: "Progressing"

ReplicationControllerList

ReplicationControllerList represents a collection of ReplicationController resources. This is the response format when listing multiple controllers for your Django application components across different services or environments.

Syntax
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationControllerList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: "12345"
  selfLink: /api/v1/replicationcontrollers
items:
- apiVersion: v1
  kind: ReplicationController
  metadata:
    name: anihpj-django-rc
    namespace: default
  spec:
    replicas: 3
    selector:
      app: anihpj
      component: web
  status:
    replicas: 3
    readyReplicas: 3
- apiVersion: v1
  kind: ReplicationController
  metadata:
    name: jobpost-worker-rc
    namespace: default
  spec:
    replicas: 2
    selector:
      app: anihpj
      component: worker
  status:
    replicas: 2
    readyReplicas: 2
Parameters Description
  • apiVersion (string, required): API version, always "v1" for ReplicationControllerList
  • kind (string, required): Resource type, always "ReplicationControllerList"
  • metadata (ListMeta): Standard list metadata containing resourceVersion and continuation token
  • items ([]ReplicationController, required): Array of ReplicationController objects in the list
Example 1: List All Django ReplicationControllers

This example demonstrates how to retrieve and display all ReplicationControllers as a ReplicationControllerList in YAML format.

# Get all ReplicationControllers as YAML ReplicationControllerList
kubectl get rc -o yaml
apiVersion: v1 kind: ReplicationControllerList metadata: resourceVersion: "98765" items: - apiVersion: v1 kind: ReplicationController metadata: creationTimestamp: "2025-09-08T10:00:00Z" labels: app: anihpj component: web name: anihpj-django-rc namespace: default resourceVersion: "98745" uid: 12345678-1234-1234-1234-123456789abc spec: replicas: 3 selector: app: anihpj component: web template: metadata: labels: app: anihpj component: web spec: containers: - image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0 name: django-web ports: - containerPort: 8000 protocol: TCP status: availableReplicas: 3 fullyLabeledReplicas: 3 observedGeneration: 1 readyReplicas: 3 replicas: 3 - apiVersion: v1 kind: ReplicationController metadata: creationTimestamp: "2025-09-08T10:05:00Z" labels: app: anihpj component: worker name: jobpost-worker-rc namespace: default resourceVersion: "98750" uid: 87654321-4321-4321-4321-cba987654321 spec: replicas: 2 selector: app: anihpj component: worker template: metadata: labels: app: anihpj component: worker spec: containers: - image: anihpj/jobpost-worker:v1.0.0 name: django-worker command: ["python", "manage.py", "process_jobs"] status: availableReplicas: 2 fullyLabeledReplicas: 2 observedGeneration: 1 readyReplicas: 2 replicas: 2

Operations

Operations Overview

Read - GET single ReplicationController details
List - GET multiple ReplicationControllers
Create - POST new ReplicationController
Update - PUT/PATCH existing ReplicationController
Delete - DELETE ReplicationController resources
Status - Manage ReplicationController status subresource
Patch - Partially update ReplicationController
Watch - Monitor ReplicationController changes

Operations allow you to interact with ReplicationController resources through the Kubernetes API. These operations enable you to manage Django application deployments, scale services, and monitor health status.

Read ReplicationController

HTTP Request

Method - GET
Path - /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}
Response - ReplicationController object
Use Case - Retrieve Django app deployment details

Read the specified ReplicationController to get complete configuration and status information for your Django application deployment.

Syntax
kubectl get replicationcontroller {name} -o yaml
kubectl get rc {name} -o json
kubectl describe replicationcontroller {name}
HTTP API Syntax
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}
Accept: application/json
Authorization: Bearer {token}
Parameters
  • name (string, required): Name of the ReplicationController
  • namespace (string, required): Object namespace (default: "default")
  • pretty (string): Pretty-print the output
Return Value
  • 200 (ReplicationController): OK - Returns the complete ReplicationController object
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
5 Django Service Examples
Example 1: Skills Model ReplicationController (jobpost app)
# Get Skills RC configuration in YAML format
kubectl get rc anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc -o yaml
apiVersion: v1 kind: ReplicationController metadata: name: anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc namespace: default labels: app: anihpj component: jobpost service: skills spec: replicas: 2 selector: app: anihpj component: jobpost service: skills template: metadata: labels: app: anihpj component: jobpost service: skills spec: containers: - name: jobpost-skills image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0 ports: - containerPort: 8000 env: - name: DJANGO_APP value: "jobpost" - name: MODEL_FOCUS value: "skills" status: replicas: 2 readyReplicas: 2 availableReplicas: 2
Example 2: Author Model Management Service (jobpost app)
# Get detailed description of User RC

Read Status ReplicationController

HTTP Request

Method - GET
Path - /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}/status
Response - ReplicationController object
Use Case - Monitor Django app deployment status

Read status of the specified ReplicationController to monitor the health and current state of your Django application deployment.

Syntax
kubectl get rc {name} -o jsonpath='{.status}'
kubectl get rc {name} --show-labels
HTTP API Syntax
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}/status
Accept: application/json
Authorization: Bearer {token}
Parameters
  • name (string, required): Name of the ReplicationController
  • namespace (string, required): Object namespace
  • pretty (string): Pretty-print the output
Return Value
  • 200 (ReplicationController): OK - Returns the ReplicationController object with status information
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
5 Django Status Examples
Example 1: Skills Model Service Status (jobpost app)
# Get Skills RC status in formatted JSON
kubectl get rc anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc -o jsonpath='{.status}' | python -m json.tool

Example 2: Author Model Service Status (jobpost app)

Example 3: Location Model Service Status (jobpost app)

Example 4: JobPost Model Main Service Status (jobpost app)

List ReplicationControllers

HTTP Request

Method - GET
Path - /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers
Response - ReplicationControllerList
Use Case - List all Django deployments

List all ReplicationControllers in a namespace to get an overview of your Django application deployments and their current status.

Syntax
kubectl get replicationcontrollers
kubectl get rc -l app={label}
kubectl get rc -o wide
HTTP API Syntax
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers
Accept: application/json
Authorization: Bearer {token}
Parameters
  • namespace (string, required): Object namespace
  • labelSelector (string): Label selector for filtering
  • fieldSelector (string): Field selector for filtering
  • limit (integer): Maximum number of results
  • continue (string): Continue token for pagination
  • watch (boolean): Watch for changes to objects
Example 1: List All Django ReplicationControllers

This example shows how to list ReplicationControllers filtered by application labels in a specific namespace.

This example shows advanced listing with JSON path queries to extract specific information from multiple ReplicationControllers.

# Extract specific fields from all anihpj ReplicationControllers
kubectl get rc -l app=anihpj -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}{"\t"}{.spec.replicas}{"\t"}{.status.readyReplicas}{"\t"}{.spec.template.spec.containers[0].image}{"\n"}{end}'
anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc 3 3 anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.2.0 anihpj-jobpost-author-rc 2 2 anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.1.0 anihpj-location-prod-rc 4 4 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.0.0
# Get creation timestamps and current status
kubectl get rc -l app=anihpj -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}{": created "}{.metadata.creationTimestamp}{", replicas: "}{.status.replicas}{"/"}{.spec.replicas}{"\n"}{end}'
anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc: created 2025-09-08T09:35:00Z, replicas: 3/3 anihpj-jobpost-author-rc: created 2025-09-08T09:40:00Z, replicas: 2/2 anihpj-location-prod-rc: created 2025-09-08T09:45:00Z, replicas: 4/4

List All Namespaces ReplicationController

HTTP Request

Method - GET
Path - /api/v1/replicationcontrollers
Response - ReplicationControllerList
Use Case - List Django deployments across all namespaces

List or watch objects of kind ReplicationController across all namespaces to get a cluster-wide view of Django deployments.

Syntax
kubectl get rc --all-namespaces
kubectl get rc -A -o wide
HTTP API Syntax
GET /api/v1/replicationcontrollers
Accept: application/json
Authorization: Bearer {token}
Parameters
  • allowWatchBookmarks (boolean): Allow watch bookmarks
  • continue (string): Continue token for pagination
  • fieldSelector (string): Field selector for filtering
  • labelSelector (string): Label selector for filtering
  • limit (integer): Maximum number of results
  • pretty (string): Pretty-print the output
  • resourceVersion (string): Resource version for consistency
  • resourceVersionMatch (string): Resource version match strategy
  • sendInitialEvents (boolean): Send initial events for watch
  • timeoutSeconds (integer): Timeout for the request
  • watch (boolean): Watch for changes
Return Value
  • 200 (ReplicationControllerList): OK - Returns list of ReplicationController objects across all namespaces
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
5 Django Cross-Namespace Examples
Example 1: Skills Model Across All Namespaces (jobpost app)

Create ReplicationController

HTTP Request

Method - POST
Path - /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers
Body - ReplicationController object
Response - Created ReplicationController

Create a new ReplicationController to deploy your Django application with the specified configuration and replica count.

Syntax
kubectl create -f replicationcontroller.yaml
kubectl apply -f replicationcontroller.yaml
echo "{yaml-content}" | kubectl create -f -
HTTP API Syntax
POST /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers
Content-Type: application/yaml
Authorization: Bearer {token}

{ReplicationController-manifest}
Example 1: Create Skills Model Service (jobpost app)
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: skills
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: skills
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost
        service: skills
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-skills
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: DJANGO_APP
          value: "jobpost"
        - name: MODEL_FOCUS
          value: "skills"
        - name: DB_PATH
          value: "sqlite:///db.sqlite3"
# Create Skills model ReplicationController
kubectl create -f anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc.yaml
replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc created
Example 2: Create Author Model Service (jobpost app)
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-author-rc
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: author
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: author
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost
        service: author
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-author
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: DJANGO_APP
          value: "jobpost"
        - name: MODEL_FOCUS
          value: "author"
        - name: DB_PATH
          value: "sqlite:///db.sqlite3"
        - name: USER_RELATION
          value: "onetoone"
# Apply Author model ReplicationController
kubectl apply -f anihpj-jobpost-author-rc.yaml
replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-author-rc created
Example 3: Create Location Model Service (jobpost app)

  name: anihpj-jobpost-location-rc

Update ReplicationController

HTTP Request

Method - PUT
Path - /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}
Body - Complete ReplicationController object
Response - Updated ReplicationController

Replace the entire ReplicationController specification with new configuration. Useful for major Django application updates.

Syntax
kubectl replace -f replicationcontroller.yaml
kubectl apply -f updated-replicationcontroller.yaml
HTTP API Syntax
PUT /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}
Content-Type: application/yaml
Authorization: Bearer {token}

{Updated-ReplicationController-manifest}
Example 1: Update Django App Image Version
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-django-rc
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: web
spec:
  replicas: 5  # Scaled up from 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    component: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: web
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-web
        image: anihpj/django-app:v2.0.0  # Updated version
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        resources:
          requests:
            cpu: 100m
            memory: 256Mi
kubectl replace -f anihpj-django-rc-v2.yaml
replicationcontroller/anihpj-django-rc replaced
Example 2: Update Skills API Service Configuration (jobpost app)

This example shows how to update the Skills API service configuration with new environment variables and resource limits.

# skills-api-update.yaml
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    service: skills-api
    version: v1.3.0
spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    service: skills-api
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        service: skills-api
        version: v1.3.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: skills-api
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.3.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: API_ENDPOINT
          value: "/jobpost/skills/"
        - name: CACHE_TIMEOUT
          value: "300"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "400m"
# Update the Skills API ReplicationController
kubectl replace -f skills-api-update.yaml
replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc replaced
Example 3: Update Author Management Service Scaling (jobpost app)

This example demonstrates updating the Author management service with increased replicas and updated container image.

# Get current Author RC configuration and modify it
kubectl get rc anihpj-jobpost-author-rc -o yaml > author-service-update.yaml
# Edit the file to change replicas from 2 to 5 and update image version
# Then apply the changes
kubectl replace -f author-service-update.yaml
replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-author-rc replaced
# Verify the update was successful
kubectl get rc anihpj-jobpost-author-rc -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,REPLICAS:.spec.replicas,IMAGE:.spec.template.spec.containers[0].image
NAME REPLICAS IMAGE anihpj-jobpost-author-rc 5 anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.2.0
Example 4: Update Location Service with Health Checks (jobpost app)

This example shows updating the Location service to add comprehensive health checks and monitoring.

# location-service-health-update.yaml
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-location-prod-rc
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    service: location
    environment: production
    version: v2.1.0
spec:
  replicas: 6
  selector:
    app: anihpj
    service: location
    environment: production
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        service: location
        environment: production
        version: v2.1.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: location-service
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        - containerPort: 9090
          name: metrics
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: HEALTH_CHECK_ENABLED
          value: "true"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/live/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 3
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "300Mi"
            cpu: "150m"
          limits:
            memory: "600Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
# Apply the Location service health check update
kubectl replace -f location-service-health-update.yaml
replicationcontroller/anihpj-location-prod-rc replaced
Example 5: Complete JobPost Main API Update (jobpost app)

This example demonstrates a comprehensive update to the main JobPost API service with new features, security, and performance improvements.

# Create comprehensive update using kubectl create --dry-run and then replace
kubectl create rc anihpj-jobpost-main-rc-v2 \
  --image=anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 \
  --replicas=8 \
  --dry-run=client -o yaml > jobpost-main-comprehensive-update.yaml

# Edit the file to add additional configurations
# Then replace the existing ReplicationController
kubectl replace -f jobpost-main-comprehensive-update.yaml
replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-main-rc replaced
# Monitor the rollout progress
kubectl rollout status rc/anihpj-jobpost-main-rc --timeout=300s
Waiting for rollout to finish: 2 of 8 updated replicas are available... Waiting for rollout to finish: 4 of 8 updated replicas are available... Waiting for rollout to finish: 6 of 8 updated replicas are available... deployment "anihpj-jobpost-main-rc" successfully rolled out
# Verify all replicas are running with new version
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj,service=jobpost-main -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,IMAGE:.spec.containers[0].image,STATUS:.status.phase
NAME IMAGE STATUS anihpj-jobpost-main-rc-abc123 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 Running anihpj-jobpost-main-rc-def456 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 Running anihpj-jobpost-main-rc-ghi789 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 Running anihpj-jobpost-main-rc-jkl012 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 Running anihpj-jobpost-main-rc-mno345 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 Running anihpj-jobpost-main-rc-pqr678 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 Running anihpj-jobpost-main-rc-stu901 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 Running anihpj-jobpost-main-rc-vwx234 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 Running

Update Status ReplicationController

HTTP Request

Method - PUT
Path - /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}/status
Body - ReplicationController object
Response - Updated ReplicationController

Replace status of the specified ReplicationController. This operation is typically used by controllers, not end users.

HTTP API Syntax
PUT /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}/status
Content-Type: application/yaml
Authorization: Bearer {token}

{ReplicationController-status-object}
Parameters
  • name (string, required): Name of the ReplicationController
  • namespace (string, required): Object namespace
  • body (ReplicationController, required): ReplicationController object
  • dryRun (string): Dry run mode
  • fieldManager (string): Field manager name
  • fieldValidation (string): Field validation mode
  • pretty (string): Pretty-print the output
Return Value

Returns the updated ReplicationController object with status information reflecting the current state of replicas.

  • 200 OK: ReplicationController status successfully updated
  • 400 Bad Request: Invalid ReplicationController status object
  • 401 Unauthorized: Authentication required
  • 403 Forbidden: Insufficient permissions
  • 404 Not Found: ReplicationController not found
  • 409 Conflict: Conflict with current state
  • 422 Unprocessable Entity: Invalid field values
Example 1: Update Django App Status (System Operation)
# This is typically done by Kubernetes controllers, not users
curl -X PUT \
  https://k8s-api/api/v1/namespaces/default/replicationcontrollers/anihpj-django-rc/status \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{
    "status": {
      "replicas": 3,
      "readyReplicas": 2,
      "availableReplicas": 2
    }
  }'
HTTP/1.1 200 OK { "kind": "ReplicationController", "metadata": {"name": "anihpj-django-rc"}, "status": { "replicas": 3, "readyReplicas": 2, "availableReplicas": 2 } }
Example 2: Update JobPost Processing Worker Status
# jobpost-worker-status.yaml
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: jobpost-worker-rc
  namespace: default
status:
  replicas: 2
  readyReplicas: 2
  availableReplicas: 2
  conditions:
  - type: ReplicaFailure
    status: "False"
    reason: "PodsRunning"
    message: "All replicas are running successfully"
# Replace the status subresource of the worker ReplicationController
kubectl replace --subresource=status -f jobpost-worker-status.yaml
replicationcontroller/jobpost-worker-rc status updated

    "status": {
      "replicas": 5,

    }
  }'
HTTP/1.1 200 OK { "kind": "ReplicationController", "metadata": { "name": "skills-processor-rc", "namespace": "anihpj-production" }, "status": { "replicas": 5, "readyReplicas": 4, "availableReplicas": 4, "observedGeneration": 3 } }

Patch ReplicationController

HTTP Request

Method - PATCH
Path - /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}
Body - Partial update object
Response - Updated ReplicationController

Partially update specific fields of a ReplicationController. Most commonly used for scaling Django applications.

Syntax
kubectl scale rc {name} --replicas={count}
kubectl patch rc {name} -p '{patch-object}'
kubectl patch rc {name} --type merge -p '{patch-data}'
HTTP API Syntax
PATCH /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}
Content-Type: application/strategic-merge-patch+json
Authorization: Bearer {token}

{Patch-object}
Example 1: Scale Django Application

This example demonstrates how to scale a Django ReplicationController both using the scale command and patch operations.

# Scale Django ReplicationController to 5 replicas
kubectl scale rc anihpj-django-rc --replicas=5
replicationcontroller/anihpj-django-rc scaled
# Patch Django ReplicationController using JSON to set replicas to 5
kubectl patch rc anihpj-django-rc -p '{"spec":{"replicas":5}}'
replicationcontroller/anihpj-django-rc patched
Example 2: Update JobPost Worker Environment
kubectl patch rc jobpost-worker-rc -p '{
  "spec": {
    "template": {
      "spec": {
        "containers": [{
          "name": "django-worker",
          "env": [
            {"name": "WORKER_CONCURRENCY", "value": "8"},
            {"name": "LOG_LEVEL", "value": "INFO"}
          ]
        }]
      }
    }
  }
}'
replicationcontroller/jobpost-worker-rc patched

# System-level operation typically done by controllers

Delete ReplicationController

HTTP Request

Method - DELETE
Path - /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}
Response - Status of deletion
Options - Cascade deletion settings

Delete a ReplicationController and optionally its managed pods. Critical for Django application cleanup and resource management.

Syntax
kubectl delete rc {name}
kubectl delete rc {name} --cascade=orphan
kubectl delete -f replicationcontroller.yaml
HTTP API Syntax
DELETE /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}
Content-Type: application/json
Authorization: Bearer {token}

{
  "kind": "DeleteOptions",
  "propagationPolicy": "Foreground"
}
Parameters
  • propagationPolicy (string): "Foreground", "Background", or "Orphan"
  • gracePeriodSeconds (integer): Grace period for pod termination
  • orphanDependents (boolean): Deprecated. Use propagationPolicy
Return Value

Returns the status of the deletion operation with information about the ReplicationController removal.

  • 200 OK: ReplicationController successfully deleted
  • 400 Bad Request: Invalid delete options
  • 401 Unauthorized: Authentication required
  • 403 Forbidden: Insufficient permissions to delete
  • 404 Not Found: ReplicationController not found
  • 409 Conflict: Conflict with current state during deletion
Example 1: Delete Django RC and Pods
kubectl delete rc anihpj-django-rc
replicationcontroller "anihpj-django-rc" deleted
# Check if pods are still running after RC deletion (should be none)
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj,component=web
No resources found in default namespace.
Example 2: Delete RC but Keep Pods Running
# Delete ReplicationController but keep the pods running (orphan cascade)
kubectl delete rc jobpost-worker-rc --cascade=orphan
replicationcontroller "jobpost-worker-rc" deleted
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj,component=worker
NAME READY STATUS RESTARTS AGE jobpost-worker-rc-k7x3m 1/1 Running 0 10m jobpost-worker-rc-m9p2n 1/1 Running 0 10m
Example 3: Delete Skills Processing RC with Custom Grace Period
# Delete with longer grace period for graceful shutdown
kubectl delete rc skills-processor-rc --grace-period=60
replicationcontroller "skills-processor-rc" deleted
# Verify deletion
kubectl get rc skills-processor-rc
Error from server (NotFound): replicationcontrollers "skills-processor-rc" not found
Example 4: Force Delete Stuck ReplicationController
# Force delete if RC is stuck in terminating state
kubectl delete rc user-auth-rc --force --grace-period=0
warning: Immediate deletion does not wait for confirmation that the running resource has been terminated. The resource may continue to run on the cluster indefinitely. replicationcontroller "user-auth-rc" force deleted
# Clean up any remaining pods manually if needed
kubectl delete pods -l app=anihpj,component=auth --force --grace-period=0
Example 5: Delete Location Service RC via API
# Delete using direct API call with propagation policy
curl -X DELETE \
  https://k8s-api/api/v1/namespaces/anihpj-services/replicationcontrollers/location-service-rc \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{
    "kind": "DeleteOptions",
    "apiVersion": "v1",
    "propagationPolicy": "Foreground",
    "gracePeriodSeconds": 30
  }'
HTTP/1.1 200 OK { "kind": "Status", "apiVersion": "v1", "status": "Success", "details": { "name": "location-service-rc", "kind": "replicationcontrollers", "uid": "12345678-1234-1234-1234-123456789012" } }

Delete Collection ReplicationController

HTTP Request

Method - DELETE
Path - /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers
Body - DeleteOptions
Response - Status

Delete collection of ReplicationController resources matching specified criteria. Useful for bulk cleanup of Django deployments.

Syntax
kubectl delete rc -l {label-selector}
kubectl delete rc --all
kubectl delete rc -l app=anihpj
HTTP API Syntax
DELETE /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers
Content-Type: application/json
Authorization: Bearer {token}

{
  "kind": "DeleteOptions",
  "propagationPolicy": "Foreground"
}
Parameters
  • namespace (string, required): Object namespace
  • body (DeleteOptions): Delete options
  • continue (string): Continue token for pagination
  • dryRun (string): Dry run mode
  • fieldSelector (string): Field selector for filtering
  • gracePeriodSeconds (integer): Grace period for termination
  • ignoreStoreReadErrorWithClusterBreakingPotential (boolean): Ignore store read errors
  • labelSelector (string): Label selector for filtering
  • limit (integer): Maximum number to delete
  • pretty (string): Pretty-print the output
  • propagationPolicy (string): Propagation policy
  • resourceVersion (string): Resource version
  • resourceVersionMatch (string): Resource version match strategy
  • sendInitialEvents (boolean): Send initial events
  • timeoutSeconds (integer): Timeout for the operation
Example 1: Delete All Django ReplicationControllers
kubectl delete rc -l app=anihpj
replicationcontroller "anihpj-django-rc" deleted replicationcontroller "jobpost-worker-rc" deleted
Example 2: Delete All Worker ReplicationControllers
kubectl delete rc -l component=worker --dry-run=client
replicationcontroller "jobpost-worker-rc" deleted (dry run) replicationcontroller "skills-processor-rc" deleted (dry run)
✅ Best Practices for Django Applications:
  • Use meaningful names like "anihpj-web-rc" or "jobpost-worker-rc"
  • Set appropriate resource requests/limits for Django containers
  • Include health checks for Django application endpoints
  • Use ConfigMaps for Django settings and Secrets for sensitive data
  • Consider using Deployments instead of ReplicationController for production
Example 3: Delete Skills and Author Services (jobpost app)

This example shows how to delete specific service ReplicationControllers using label selectors for Skills and Author services.

# Delete Skills and Author service ReplicationControllers
kubectl delete rc -l "service in (skills-api,author-mgmt)"
replicationcontroller "anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc" deleted replicationcontroller "anihpj-jobpost-author-rc" deleted
# Verify deletion completed
kubectl get rc -l "service in (skills-api,author-mgmt)"
No resources found in default namespace.
Example 4: Delete All Development Environment RCs (jobpost app)

This example demonstrates bulk deletion of all development environment ReplicationControllers with confirmation and cleanup verification.

kubectl get rc -l environment=development --show-labels

# Delete all development environment ReplicationControllers

# Check for any remaining development pods

Example 5: Delete All Inactive JobPost Services (jobpost app)

This example shows advanced deletion using field selectors and multiple criteria for cleaning up inactive or terminated ReplicationControllers.

# List all RCs with their current status
kubectl get rc -l app=anihpj -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,DESIRED:.spec.replicas,CURRENT:.status.replicas,READY:.status.readyReplicas,AGE:.metadata.creationTimestamp
NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY AGE anihpj-jobpost-skills-rc 3 3 3 2025-09-08T09:35:00Z anihpj-jobpost-author-rc 2 2 2 2025-09-08T09:40:00Z anihpj-location-prod-rc 4 4 4 2025-09-08T09:45:00Z anihpj-old-api-rc 0 0 0 2025-09-07T15:30:00Z anihpj-test-rc 0 0 0 2025-09-07T14:20:00Z 
# Delete RCs with zero desired replicas (inactive services)
kubectl delete rc -l app=anihpj --field-selector spec.replicas=0
replicationcontroller "anihpj-old-api-rc" deleted replicationcontroller "anihpj-test-rc" deleted
# Verify only active services remain
kubectl get rc -l app=anihpj --show-labels

Deployment

Deployment Overview

DeploymentSpec - Desired state specification
DeploymentStatus - Current observed status
DeploymentList - Collection of deployments
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: Deployment v1 API | API Version: apps/v1

Deployment enables declarative updates for Pods and ReplicaSets, providing advanced deployment strategies for Django applications.

Full Description

Deployment is the recommended way to deploy stateless applications in Kubernetes. It provides declarative updates for Pods and ReplicaSets, enabling rolling updates, rollbacks, and scaling for your anihpj Django application. Unlike ReplicationController, Deployments support advanced deployment strategies and are the modern standard for managing stateless workloads in production environments.

For Django applications, Deployments are ideal for web servers, API services, and background workers that don't require persistent state. They automatically manage ReplicaSets and provide features like rolling updates, which allow you to update your jobpost application without downtime.

Syntax

# Create a Deployment from YAML file
kubectl create -f deployment.yaml
# Create a Deployment directly with kubectl
kubectl create deployment {name} --image={image}
# List all Deployments
kubectl get deployments
# List all Deployments (short form)
kubectl get deploy
# Get detailed information about a specific Deployment
kubectl describe deployment {name}
# Get detailed information about a specific Deployment (short form)
kubectl describe deploy {name}
# Scale Deployment to specified number of replicas
kubectl scale deployment {name} --replicas={count}
# Check the rollout status of a Deployment
kubectl rollout status deployment/{name}
# View the rollout history of a Deployment
kubectl rollout history deployment/{name}
# Rollback to previous version of a Deployment
kubectl rollout undo deployment/{name}
# Rollback to specific revision of a Deployment
kubectl rollout undo deployment/{name} --to-revision={number}
# Pause a deployment rollout
kubectl rollout pause deployment/{name}
# Resume a paused deployment rollout
kubectl rollout resume deployment/{name}
# Delete a specific Deployment
kubectl delete deployment {name}
# Delete a specific Deployment (short form)
kubectl delete deploy {name}

YAML Structure

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-django-deployment
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: web
    version: v1.0.0
spec:
  replicas: 3
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
      maxSurge: 1
  minReadySeconds: 10
  revisionHistoryLimit: 10
  progressDeadlineSeconds: 600
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj
      component: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: web
        version: v1.0.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-web
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: django-port
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-secrets
              key: database-url
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
          timeoutSeconds: 5
          failureThreshold: 3
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
          timeoutSeconds: 3
          successThreshold: 1
          failureThreshold: 3

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: Always "apps/v1" for Deployment. This indicates the API version being used.
  • kind: Must be "Deployment" to specify the resource type.
  • metadata.name: Unique name for the Deployment within the namespace. Use descriptive names like "anihpj-django-deployment".
  • metadata.namespace: Kubernetes namespace where the Deployment will be created. Defaults to "default".
  • metadata.labels: Key-value pairs for organizing and selecting Deployments. Useful for grouping Django app components.
  • spec.replicas: Number of desired pod replicas. For Django apps, start with 2-3 for high availability.
  • spec.selector.matchLabels: Label selector to identify which pods belong to this Deployment. Must match template labels.
  • spec.template: Pod template specification that defines how new pods should be created.
  • spec.strategy: Deployment strategy (RollingUpdate or Recreate). RollingUpdate is recommended for Django apps.
  • spec.strategy.rollingUpdate.maxUnavailable: Maximum number of pods that can be unavailable during update.
  • spec.strategy.rollingUpdate.maxSurge: Maximum number of pods that can be created above desired number during update.
  • spec.minReadySeconds: Minimum seconds a pod must be ready before considered available. Important for Django apps with startup time.
  • spec.revisionHistoryLimit: Number of old ReplicaSets to retain for rollback. Defaults to 10.
  • spec.progressDeadlineSeconds: Maximum time in seconds for deployment to make progress before considered failed.

Return Value

Returns the Deployment object with its current state, including status information about replicas, conditions, and deployment progress.

  • 200 OK: Deployment successfully created/updated
  • 201 Created: Deployment successfully created
  • 400 Bad Request: Invalid Deployment specification
  • 401 Unauthorized: Authentication required
  • 403 Forbidden: Insufficient permissions
  • 404 Not Found: Namespace not found
  • 409 Conflict: Deployment already exists
  • 422 Unprocessable Entity: Invalid field values

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Skills API Deployment (jobpost app)

This example demonstrates deploying a Deployment for the Skills API service (/jobpost/skills/), providing JSON endpoints for managing job skills in the anihpj Django project with rolling update strategy.

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: jobpost
    service: skills-api
spec:
  replicas: 3
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
      maxSurge: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj
      component: jobpost
      service: skills-api
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost
        service: skills-api
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-skills
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.2.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_APP
          value: "jobpost"
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: SERVICE_TYPE
          value: "skills_api"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /jobpost/skills/health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 45
          periodSeconds: 30
# Apply the Skills API Deployment
kubectl apply -f anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment.yaml
# Check deployment status and rollout progress
kubectl rollout status deployment/anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment
# Get deployment details
kubectl get deployment anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment -o wide
deployment.apps/anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment created Waiting for deployment "anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment" rollout to finish: 0 of 3 updated replicas are available... Waiting for deployment "anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment" rollout to finish: 1 of 3 updated replicas are available... Waiting for deployment "anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment" rollout to finish: 2 of 3 updated replicas are available... deployment "anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment" successfully rolled out NAME READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE AGE CONTAINERS IMAGES SELECTOR anihpj-jobpost-skills-deployment 3/3 3 3 2m jobpost-skills anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.2.0 app=anihpj,component=jobpost,service=skills-api
Example 2: Author Management Deployment (jobpost app)

This example shows creating a Deployment for Author management service with configurable rolling update strategy and health checks for anihpj Django application.

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-author-mgmt-deployment
  namespace: production
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: author
    service: management
spec:
  replicas: 2
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 0
      maxSurge: 1
  minReadySeconds: 30
  revisionHistoryLimit: 5
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj
      component: author
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: author
        service: management
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: author-mgmt
        image: anihpj/author-service:v2.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.author_production"
        - name: AUTHOR_SERVICE_MODE
          value: "management"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "400m"
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /author/ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 15
          periodSeconds: 10
# Create the Author Management Deployment in production namespace
kubectl apply -f anihpj-author-mgmt-deployment.yaml -n production
# Watch the rollout progress in real-time
kubectl rollout status deployment/anihpj-author-mgmt-deployment -n production --watch
# Check deployment history and revisions
kubectl rollout history deployment/anihpj-author-mgmt-deployment -n production

Example 4: JobPost Main API Deployment with Rollback Strategy

This example shows how to deploy the main JobPost API service and demonstrate rollback capabilities when issues are detected.

kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-api-deployment
  namespace: api-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: api
    service: jobpost-main
spec:
  replicas: 5
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 20%
      maxSurge: 2
  minReadySeconds: 20
  progressDeadlineSeconds: 300
  revisionHistoryLimit: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj
      service: jobpost-main

        app: anihpj
        service: jobpost-main

        image: anihpj/jobpost-main-api:v3.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: api-port
        env:

          value: "anihpj.settings.api_production"
        - name: API_VERSION
          value: "v3.0.0"

          value: "main_api"

          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"

            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "600m"

          httpGet:
            path: /jobpost/api/health/
            port: 8000

          periodSeconds: 30

            path: /jobpost/api/ready/

          initialDelaySeconds: 15
          periodSeconds: 10

    Example 1: Create Django Web Deployment

    # anihpj-web-deployment.yaml

  name: anihpj-web-deployment
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: web
    version: v1.0.0
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj
      component: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: web
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-web
        image: anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: django-port
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: DB_PATH
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-secrets
              key: database-url
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"

    Example 5: Location Service Deployment with Advanced Configuration

    This example demonstrates an advanced Location service Deployment with custom namespaces, ConfigMap volumes, and comprehensive labeling.

    # location-service-deployment.yaml
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: location-service-deployment
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: microservice
    service: location
    version: v2.3.0
  annotations:
    deployment.kubernetes.io/revision: "1"
    kubernetes.io/change-cause: "Initial deployment of location service v2.3.0"
spec:
  replicas: 6
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
      maxSurge: 1
  minReadySeconds: 15
  revisionHistoryLimit: 5
  progressDeadlineSeconds: 300
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj
      component: microservice
      service: location
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: microservice
        service: location
        version: v2.3.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: location-service
        image: anihpj/location-service:v2.3.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: location-port
          protocol: TCP
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.location_production"
        - name: DB_PATH
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: location-config
              key: database-url
        - name: REDIS_URL
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: location-config
              key: redis-url
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "600m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /location/health/
            port: 8000
            scheme: HTTP
          initialDelaySeconds: 60
          periodSeconds: 30
          timeoutSeconds: 10
          successThreshold: 1
          failureThreshold: 3
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /location/ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 10
          periodSeconds: 10
          timeoutSeconds: 5
          successThreshold: 1
          failureThreshold: 3
        volumeMounts:
        - name: location-config
          mountPath: /app/config
          readOnly: true
      volumes:
      - name: location-config
        configMap:
          name: location-config
    # Apply the location service Deployment from YAML file
kubectl apply -f location-service-deployment.yaml
    deployment.apps/location-service-deployment created
    # Monitor deployment progress
kubectl rollout status deployment/location-service-deployment -n anihpj-services
