    ✅ Deployment Best Practices for Django Applications:
    • Use Deployments instead of ReplicationControllers for production Django apps
    • Set appropriate rolling update strategy (maxUnavailable, maxSurge)
    • Configure health checks (liveness and readiness probes) for Django endpoints
    • Set resource requests and limits based on Django application requirements
    • Use meaningful labels and annotations for better organization
    • Keep revision history limit reasonable (5-10) to avoid cluttering
    • Set appropriate progressDeadlineSeconds for deployment timeout

    DeploymentSpec

    DeploymentSpec is a description of the deployment specification. It defines the desired state for a Deployment object, including the number of replicas, the pod template, and the update strategy. This specification ensures that the deployment maintains the desired number of pods and can perform rolling updates when changes are needed.

    API Definition

    Group: apps
    Version: v1
    Kind: DeploymentSpec
    Scope: Namespaced

    Syntax

    # Create deployment with custom spec from YAML file
kubectl apply -f deployment-spec.yaml

# Update deployment spec directly with kubectl patch
kubectl patch deployment my-deployment -p '{"spec":{"replicas":5}}'

# Get deployment spec details in YAML format
kubectl get deployment my-deployment -o yaml | grep -A 20 "spec:"

# Scale deployment by modifying spec replicas
kubectl scale deployment my-deployment --replicas=3

# Set deployment spec strategy (RollingUpdate/Recreate)
kubectl patch deployment my-deployment -p '{"spec":{"strategy":{"type":"RollingUpdate"}}}'

    YAML Structure

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: example-deployment
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 3                    # Number of desired pods
  selector:                      # Label selector for pods
    matchLabels:
      app: example-app
  template:                      # Pod template specification
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: example-app
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: app-container
        image: nginx:1.21
        ports:
        - containerPort: 80
  strategy:                      # Update strategy
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
      maxSurge: 1
  revisionHistoryLimit: 10       # Number of old ReplicaSets to retain
  progressDeadlineSeconds: 600   # Maximum time for deployment to progress
  paused: false                  # Whether deployment is paused

    Parameters

    replicas integer

    Number of desired pods. This is a pointer to distinguish between explicit zero and not specified. Defaults to 1.

    selector LabelSelector

    Label selector for pods. Existing ReplicaSets whose pods are selected by this will be affected by this deployment.

    template PodTemplateSpec

    Template describes the pods that will be created. This is required.

    strategy DeploymentStrategy

    The deployment strategy to use to replace existing pods with new ones.

    revisionHistoryLimit integer

    Number of old ReplicaSets to retain to allow rollback. This is a pointer to distinguish between explicit zero and not specified. Defaults to 10.

    progressDeadlineSeconds integer

    The maximum time in seconds for a deployment to make progress before it is considered to be failed.

    paused boolean

    Indicates that the deployment is paused. Defaults to false.

    minReadySeconds integer

    Minimum number of seconds for which a newly created pod should be ready without any of its container crashing.

    Return Value

    Returns a DeploymentSpec object containing the deployment specification with all configured parameters for pod management and update strategies.

    5 Practical Django Examples

    Example 1: Basic Django App DeploymentSpec

    This example shows how to create a basic anihpj Django deployment spec with standard configuration for the jobpost application.

    # anihpj-jobpost-spec.yaml
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-deployment
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-jobpost
    component: web
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-jobpost
      tier: frontend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost
        tier: frontend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-container
        image: anihpj/jobpost:v1.2.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: url
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
      maxSurge: 1
  revisionHistoryLimit: 5
  progressDeadlineSeconds: 300
    # Apply the JobPost deployment spec
kubectl apply -f anihpj-jobpost-spec.yaml
# Check deployment spec details
kubectl get deployment anihpj-jobpost-deployment -o jsonpath='{.spec}' | jq
# Monitor rollout based on spec configuration
kubectl rollout status deployment/anihpj-jobpost-deployment -n anihpj-services
# Verify spec replicas are maintained
kubectl get deployment anihpj-jobpost-deployment -o jsonpath='{.spec.replicas}' -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-jobpost-deployment created { "replicas": 3, "selector": { "matchLabels": { "app": "anihpj-jobpost", "tier": "frontend" } }, "strategy": { "type": "RollingUpdate", "rollingUpdate": { "maxSurge": 1, "maxUnavailable": 1 } } } Waiting for deployment "anihpj-jobpost-deployment" rollout to finish: 0 of 3 updated replicas are available... deployment "anihpj-jobpost-deployment" successfully rolled out 3
    Example 2: High Availability Django API DeploymentSpec

    This example demonstrates a high-availability anihpj Django deployment spec with multiple replicas and resource constraints.

    # anihpj-api-ha-spec.yaml
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-api-ha-deployment
  namespace: anihpj-production
  labels:
    app: anihpj-api
    environment: production

  replicas: 6
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-api
      version: stable

    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-api
        version: stable
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: api-container
        image: anihpj/api:stable-v2.1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 15
          periodSeconds: 5
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 25%
      maxSurge: 25%
  revisionHistoryLimit: 10
  progressDeadlineSeconds: 600
  minReadySeconds: 30
    # Deploy high-availability API spec

    deployment.apps/anihpj-api-ha-deployment created deployment.apps/anihpj-api-ha-deployment scaled deployment.apps/anihpj-api-ha-deployment patched StrategyType: RollingUpdate MinReadySeconds: 30 RollingUpdateStrategy: 0 max unavailable, 25% max surge Pod Template: Labels: app=anihpj-api version=stable Containers: api-container: Image: anihpj/api:stable-v2.1.0
    Example 3: Canary Deployment Spec for Django Updates

    This example shows how to configure a canary deployment spec for anihpj Django application updates with controlled rollout.

    # anihpj-canary-spec.yaml
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-canary-deployment
  namespace: anihpj-staging
  labels:
    app: anihpj-web
    deployment-type: canary
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-web
      version: canary
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-web
        version: canary
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: web-container
        image: anihpj/web:canary-v2.2.0-rc1
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DEPLOYMENT_TYPE
          value: "canary"
        - name: FEATURE_FLAGS
          value: "new_ui=true,enhanced_search=true"
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 0
      maxSurge: 1
  revisionHistoryLimit: 15
  progressDeadlineSeconds: 900
  paused: false
    # Apply canary deployment spec
kubectl apply -f anihpj-canary-spec.yaml
# Pause deployment for manual verification
kubectl rollout pause deployment/anihpj-canary-deployment -n anihpj-staging
# Resume after testing
kubectl rollout resume deployment/anihpj-canary-deployment -n anihpj-staging
# Check canary deployment spec status
kubectl get deployment anihpj-canary-deployment -o jsonpath='{.spec.paused}' -n anihpj-staging
    deployment.apps/anihpj-canary-deployment created deployment.apps/anihpj-canary-deployment paused deployment.apps/anihpj-canary-deployment resumed false
    Example 4: Blue-Green Deployment Spec Configuration

    This example demonstrates configuring a blue-green deployment spec for anihpj Django application with environment-specific settings.

    # anihpj-blue-green-spec.yaml
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-green-deployment
  namespace: anihpj-production
  labels:
    app: anihpj-web
    environment: green
spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-web
      slot: green
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-web
        slot: green
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: web-container
        image: anihpj/web:v2.3.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: SLOT_COLOR
          value: "green"
        - name: DATABASE_POOL
          value: "green-pool"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "600m"
  strategy:
    type: Recreate
  revisionHistoryLimit: 3
  progressDeadlineSeconds: 1200
    # Deploy green environment spec
kubectl apply -f anihpj-blue-green-spec.yaml
# Wait for green deployment to be ready
kubectl rollout status deployment/anihpj-green-deployment -n anihpj-production --timeout=600s
# Switch traffic by updating service selector
kubectl patch service anihpj-web-service -p '{"spec":{"selector":{"slot":"green"}}}' -n anihpj-production
# Verify green deployment spec is active
kubectl get deployment anihpj-green-deployment -o jsonpath='{.spec.template.metadata.labels.slot}' -n anihpj-production
    deployment.apps/anihpj-green-deployment created Waiting for deployment "anihpj-green-deployment" rollout to finish: 0 of 4 updated replicas are available... deployment "anihpj-green-deployment" successfully rolled out service/anihpj-web-service patched green
    Example 5: Maintenance Mode DeploymentSpec

    This example shows how to configure a maintenance mode deployment spec for anihpj Django application during system updates.

    # anihpj-maintenance-spec.yaml
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-maintenance-deployment
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-web
    mode: maintenance
spec:
  replicas: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-web
      mode: maintenance
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-web
        mode: maintenance
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: maintenance-container
        image: anihpj/maintenance:v1.0.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: MAINTENANCE_MESSAGE
          value: "System maintenance in progress. Please try again later."
        - name: ESTIMATED_DURATION
          value: "2 hours"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "64Mi"
            cpu: "50m"
          limits:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 0
      maxSurge: 1
  revisionHistoryLimit: 2
  progressDeadlineSeconds: 180
  paused: false
    # Apply maintenance mode deployment spec
kubectl apply -f anihpj-maintenance-spec.yaml
# Scale down main application
kubectl scale deployment anihpj-web-deployment --replicas=0 -n anihpj-services
# Update service to point to maintenance deployment
kubectl patch service anihpj-web-service -p '{"spec":{"selector":{"mode":"maintenance"}}}' -n anihpj-services
# Check maintenance deployment spec status
kubectl get deployment anihpj-maintenance-deployment -o jsonpath='{.spec.replicas}' -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-maintenance-deployment created deployment.apps/anihpj-web-deployment scaled service/anihpj-web-service patched 1

    DeploymentStatus

    DeploymentStatus represents the current status of a Deployment. It provides information about the deployment's observed state, including the number of available replicas, conditions, and the current revision. This status helps monitor the health and progress of deployments in real-time.

    API Definition

    Group: apps
    Version: v1
    Kind: DeploymentStatus
    Scope: Namespaced

    Syntax

    # Get deployment status details
kubectl get deployment my-deployment -o jsonpath='{.status}'

# Watch deployment status changes in real-time
kubectl get deployment my-deployment --watch -o jsonpath='{.status.replicas}'

# Check deployment conditions
kubectl get deployment my-deployment -o jsonpath='{.status.conditions[*].type}'

# Get available replica count
kubectl get deployment my-deployment -o jsonpath='{.status.availableReplicas}'

# Check deployment rollout status
kubectl rollout status deployment/my-deployment --timeout=300s

    YAML Structure

    status:
  replicas: 3                      # Total number of non-terminated pods
  updatedReplicas: 3               # Number of non-terminated pods that have the desired template spec
  readyReplicas: 3                 # Number of pods targeted by this deployment with Ready Condition
  availableReplicas: 3             # Total number of available pods targeted by this deployment
  unavailableReplicas: 0           # Total number of unavailable pods targeted by this deployment
  observedGeneration: 2            # The generation observed by the deployment controller
  conditions:                      # Represents the latest available observations
  - type: Progressing
    status: "True"
    lastUpdateTime: "2024-01-15T10:30:45Z"
    lastTransitionTime: "2024-01-15T10:25:30Z"
    reason: NewReplicaSetAvailable
    message: "ReplicaSet \"my-deployment-7b8f9c5d6\" has successfully progressed."
  - type: Available
    status: "True"
    lastUpdateTime: "2024-01-15T10:30:45Z"
    lastTransitionTime: "2024-01-15T10:30:45Z"
    reason: MinimumReplicasAvailable
    message: "Deployment has minimum availability."
  collisionCount: 0                # Count of hash collisions for the Deployment

    Parameters

    replicas integer

    Total number of non-terminated pods targeted by this deployment (their labels match the selector).

    updatedReplicas integer

    Total number of non-terminated pods targeted by this deployment that have the desired template spec.

    readyReplicas integer

    Total number of ready pods targeted by this deployment.

    availableReplicas integer

    Total number of available pods (ready for at least minReadySeconds) targeted by this deployment.

    unavailableReplicas integer

    Total number of unavailable pods targeted by this deployment.

    conditions []DeploymentCondition

    Represents the latest available observations of a deployment's current state.

    observedGeneration integer

    The generation observed by the deployment controller.

    collisionCount integer

    Count of hash collisions for the Deployment. The Deployment controller uses this field as a collision avoidance mechanism.

    Return Value

    Returns a DeploymentStatus object containing the current state information of the deployment including replica counts, conditions, and generation details.

    DeploymentList

    DeploymentList is a list of deployments. It contains an array of Deployment items and metadata about the list itself. This resource is typically used when querying multiple deployments across namespaces or when performing batch operations on deployments.

    API Definition

    Group: apps
    Version: v1
    Kind: DeploymentList
    Scope: Namespaced

    Syntax

    # List all deployments in current namespace
kubectl get deployments

# List all deployments across all namespaces
kubectl get deployments --all-namespaces

# Get deployment list in YAML format
kubectl get deployments -o yaml

# List deployments with specific labels
kubectl get deployments -l app=anihpj

# List deployments with custom columns
kubectl get deployments -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,REPLICAS:.spec.replicas,READY:.status.readyReplicas

    YAML Structure

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DeploymentList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: "12345"
  selfLink: /apis/apps/v1/deployments
items:
- apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: Deployment
  metadata:
    name: anihpj-web-deployment
    namespace: anihpj-services
    labels:
      app: anihpj-web
  spec:
    replicas: 3
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        app: anihpj-web
    template:
      # Pod template specification
  status:
    replicas: 3
    readyReplicas: 3
    availableReplicas: 3
- apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: Deployment
  metadata:
    name: anihpj-api-deployment
    namespace: anihpj-services
    labels:
      app: anihpj-api
  spec:
    replicas: 5
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        app: anihpj-api
    template:
      # Pod template specification
  status:
    replicas: 5
    readyReplicas: 5
    availableReplicas: 5

    Parameters

    apiVersion string

    APIVersion defines the versioned schema of this representation of an object. Always "apps/v1" for DeploymentList.

    kind string

    Kind is a string value representing the REST resource this object represents. Always "DeploymentList".

    metadata ListMeta

    Standard list metadata containing resource version and self link information.

    items []Deployment

    Items is the list of deployments. Each item is a complete Deployment object.

    Return Value

    Returns a DeploymentList object containing an array of Deployment objects and associated metadata for list operations.

    Example 4: Batch Operations on anihpj Deployment Lists

    This example demonstrates performing batch operations on a list of anihpj Django deployments for maintenance tasks.

    # Scale all anihpj deployments in staging environment
kubectl get deployments -n anihpj-staging -l project=anihpj -o name | xargs -I {} kubectl scale {} --replicas=1

# Update image for all anihpj web deployments
kubectl get deployments -l app=anihpj-web --all-namespaces -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.namespace}{" "}{.metadata.name}{"\n"}{end}' | while read namespace name; do kubectl set image deployment/$name -n $namespace web-container=anihpj/web:v2.3.0; done

# Apply resource limits to all anihpj deployments
kubectl get deployments -l project=anihpj --all-namespaces -o json > anihpj-deployments-backup.json

# Get deployment list for backup purposes
kubectl get deployments -l project=anihpj --all-namespaces -o yaml > anihpj-deployments-$(date +%Y%m%d).yaml
    deployment.apps/anihpj-staging-deployment scaled deployment.apps/anihpj-canary-deployment scaled deployment.apps/anihpj-web-deployment image updated deployment.apps/anihpj-staging-deployment image updated # Backup file created successfully # Backup file anihpj-deployments-20240115.yaml created
    Example 5: anihpj Deployment Resource Analysis

    This example shows how to analyze resource usage and configuration across all anihpj Django deployments for optimization.

    # Analyze resource requests across all anihpj deployments
kubectl get deployments -l project=anihpj --all-namespaces -o json | jq '.items[] | {name: .metadata.name, namespace: .metadata.namespace, containers: [.spec.template.spec.containers[] | {name: .name, requests: .resources.requests, limits: .resources.limits}]}'

# Get deployment list with revision history information
kubectl get deployments -l project=anihpj --all-namespaces -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,NAMESPACE:.metadata.namespace,REVISION:.metadata.generation,HISTORY_LIMIT:.spec.revisionHistoryLimit

# Analyze deployment strategies across anihpj applications
kubectl get deployments -l project=anihpj --all-namespaces -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}{"\t"}{.spec.strategy.type}{"\t"}{.spec.strategy.rollingUpdate.maxUnavailable}{"\t"}{.spec.strategy.rollingUpdate.maxSurge}{"\n"}{end}'

    Operations

    This section covers the available operations for Deployment resources in Kubernetes. These operations allow you to create, read, update, delete, and manage Deployment objects through the Kubernetes API.

    Create

    Create a new Deployment

    Read

    Get Deployment information

    Update

    Update Deployment configuration

    Patch

    Partially update Deployment

    Delete

    Remove Deployment

    List

    List all Deployments

    Watch

    Watch Deployment changes

    Scale

    Scale Deployment replicas

    Rollout

    Manage Deployment rollouts

    Create Deployment

    Create a new Deployment resource in the specified namespace. This operation allows you to define a new deployment with the desired pod template and replica configuration.

    HTTP Request

    POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments

    kubectl Syntax

    # Create deployment from YAML file
kubectl apply -f deployment.yaml

# Create deployment directly with kubectl create
kubectl create deployment my-deployment --image=nginx:1.21 --replicas=3

# Create deployment with specific namespace
kubectl create deployment my-deployment --image=nginx:1.21 -n my-namespace

# Create deployment with resource limits
kubectl create deployment my-deployment --image=nginx:1.21 --replicas=3 --requests=cpu=100m,memory=128Mi

# Create deployment with environment variables
kubectl create deployment my-deployment --image=nginx:1.21 --env="ENV=production"

    Django Example

    Create an anihpj Django deployment for the jobpost application with proper configuration.

    # Create anihpj jobpost deployment
kubectl create deployment anihpj-jobpost --image=anihpj/jobpost:v1.2.0 --replicas=3 -n anihpj-services --env="DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE=anihpj.settings"

# Verify deployment creation
kubectl get deployment anihpj-jobpost -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-jobpost created NAME READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE AGE anihpj-jobpost 3/3 3 3 30s
    Example 2: Skills API Service Deployment

    This example demonstrates creating a Deployment for the Skills API service (/jobpost/skills/) with specific resource limits and health checks.

    # Create Skills API deployment with resource limits
kubectl create deployment anihpj-skills-api --image=anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0 --replicas=2 --port=8000 --env="MODEL_FOCUS=skills" --env="API_ENDPOINT=/jobpost/skills/" --requests=cpu=200m,memory=256Mi --limits=cpu=500m,memory=512Mi

# Apply deployment and check status
kubectl get deployment anihpj-skills-api -o wide
    deployment.apps/anihpj-skills-api created NAME READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE AGE CONTAINERS IMAGES SELECTOR anihpj-skills-api 2/2 2 2 45s jobpost-app anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0 app=anihpj-skills-api
    Example 3: Author Management Deployment

    This example shows deploying the Author management service with database connection and authentication integration.

    # Create Author management deployment with database configuration
kubectl create deployment anihpj-author-mgmt --image=anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0 --replicas=3 --env="MODEL_FOCUS=author" --env="DB_PATH=/app/db.sqlite3" --env="DJANGO_DEBUG=False"

# Scale and verify the deployment
kubectl scale deployment anihpj-author-mgmt --replicas=4 && kubectl get deployment anihpj-author-mgmt
    deployment.apps/anihpj-author-mgmt created deployment.apps/anihpj-author-mgmt scaled NAME READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE AGE anihpj-author-mgmt 4/4 4 4 1m
    Example 4: Location Service with ConfigMap

    This example illustrates creating a Location service deployment with external configuration using ConfigMaps for environment-specific settings.

    # Create ConfigMap for location service first
kubectl create configmap location-config --from-literal=GEO_API_KEY=demo-key --from-literal=LOCATION_CACHE_TTL=3600

# Create Location service deployment referencing the ConfigMap
kubectl create deployment anihpj-location-svc --image=anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0 --replicas=2 --env="MODEL_FOCUS=location"
    configmap/location-config created deployment.apps/anihpj-location-svc created
    Example 5: JobPost Main API with Persistent Storage

    This example demonstrates deploying the main JobPost API service with persistent volume claims for SQLite database storage and comprehensive configuration.

    # Create PVC for SQLite database persistence
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: v1
kind: PersistentVolumeClaim
metadata:
  name: anihpj-sqlite-pvc
spec:
  accessModes:
    - ReadWriteOnce
  resources:
    requests:
      storage: 10Gi
EOF

# Create main JobPost API deployment with PVC
kubectl create deployment anihpj-jobpost-main --image=anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0 --replicas=4 --env="DATABASE_URL=sqlite:///data/db.sqlite3" --env="DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE=anihpj.settings"
    persistentvolumeclaim/anihpj-sqlite-pvc created deployment.apps/anihpj-jobpost-main created

    Read Deployment

    Retrieve information about a specific Deployment resource, including its current status, configuration, and metadata.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Get deployment details
kubectl get deployment my-deployment

# Get deployment in YAML format
kubectl get deployment my-deployment -o yaml

# Get deployment in JSON format
kubectl get deployment my-deployment -o json

# Describe deployment with detailed information
kubectl describe deployment my-deployment

# Get specific field from deployment
kubectl get deployment my-deployment -o jsonpath='{.status.replicas}'

    Django Example

    Read anihpj Django deployment information to check status and configuration.

    # Get anihpj web deployment details
kubectl get deployment anihpj-web-deployment -n anihpj-services -o wide

# Describe anihpj API deployment
kubectl describe deployment anihpj-api-deployment -n anihpj-services
    NAME READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE AGE CONTAINERS IMAGES SELECTOR anihpj-web-deployment 3/3 3 3 2d web anihpj/web:v2.1.0 app=anihpj-web Name: anihpj-api-deployment Namespace: anihpj-services CreationTimestamp: Mon, 13 Jan 2024 10:30:45 +0000 Labels: app=anihpj-api Annotations: deployment.kubernetes.io/revision: 2 Selector: app=anihpj-api Replicas: 5 desired | 5 updated | 5 total | 5 available | 0 unavailable

    Update Deployment

    Update a Deployment resource by replacing the entire resource definition. This triggers a rolling update of the pods managed by the deployment.

    HTTP Request

    PUT /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Update deployment from modified YAML file
kubectl apply -f updated-deployment.yaml

# Update deployment image
kubectl set image deployment/my-deployment container-name=new-image:tag

# Update deployment with environment variables
kubectl set env deployment/my-deployment ENV=production

# Update deployment resources
kubectl set resources deployment my-deployment --limits=cpu=200m,memory=256Mi --requests=cpu=100m,memory=128Mi

# Replace deployment entirely
kubectl replace -f deployment.yaml

    Django Example

    Update anihpj Django deployment with new image version and configuration changes.

    # Update anihpj web deployment image
kubectl set image deployment/anihpj-web-deployment web-container=anihpj/web:v2.2.0 -n anihpj-services

# Update anihpj API deployment environment
kubectl set env deployment/anihpj-api-deployment DEBUG=False -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-web-deployment image updated deployment.apps/anihpj-api-deployment env updated
    Example 2: JobPost Service Update

    Update anihpj JobPost service deployment with new image version and resource limits for handling increased job posting volume.

    # Update JobPost deployment image to latest version
kubectl set image deployment/anihpj-jobpost-deployment jobpost-container=anihpj/jobpost-app:v3.1.0 -n anihpj-services

# Update JobPost deployment resource limits for better performance
kubectl set resources deployment anihpj-jobpost-deployment --limits=cpu=500m,memory=512Mi --requests=cpu=250m,memory=256Mi -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-jobpost-deployment image updated deployment.apps/anihpj-jobpost-deployment resource requirements updated
    Example 3: Skills Service Rolling Update

    Perform rolling update on anihpj Skills service deployment with modified application configuration and environment variables.

    # Update Skills deployment with new database connection settings
kubectl set env deployment/anihpj-skills-deployment DB_HOST=skills-db.anihpj-services.svc.cluster.local DB_PORT=5432 -n anihpj-services

# Apply updated Skills deployment configuration from file
kubectl apply -f /deployments/anihpj-skills-deployment-v2.yaml
    deployment.apps/anihpj-skills-deployment env updated deployment.apps/anihpj-skills-deployment configured
    Example 4: Author Service Multi-field Update

    Update anihpj Author service deployment with multiple changes including image version, environment variables, and replica count.

    # Update Author deployment image and set production environment
kubectl set image deployment/anihpj-author-deployment author-container=anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.8.0 -n anihpj-services
kubectl set env deployment/anihpj-author-deployment ENVIRONMENT=production CACHE_ENABLED=true -n anihpj-services

# Replace Author deployment with updated configuration
kubectl replace -f /deployments/anihpj-author-deployment-prod.yaml
    deployment.apps/anihpj-author-deployment image updated deployment.apps/anihpj-author-deployment env updated deployment.apps/anihpj-author-deployment replaced
    Example 5: Location Service Security Update

    Update anihpj Location service deployment to apply security patches and update container registry configurations.

    # Update Location deployment with security-patched image
kubectl set image deployment/anihpj-location-deployment location-container=anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.1-security -n anihpj-services

# Update Location deployment with new security environment variables
kubectl set env deployment/anihpj-location-deployment SSL_ENABLED=true CORS_ORIGINS=https://anihpj.com,https://app.anihpj.com -n anihpj-services

# Verify the update rollout status
kubectl rollout status deployment/anihpj-location-deployment -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-location-deployment image updated deployment.apps/anihpj-location-deployment env updated Waiting for deployment "anihpj-location-deployment" rollout to finish: 2 of 3 updated replicas are available... deployment "anihpj-location-deployment" successfully rolled out

    Patch Deployment

    Partially update a Deployment resource by modifying specific fields without replacing the entire resource definition.

    HTTP Request

    PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Patch deployment replicas
kubectl patch deployment my-deployment -p '{"spec":{"replicas":5}}'

# Patch deployment strategy
kubectl patch deployment my-deployment -p '{"spec":{"strategy":{"type":"RollingUpdate","rollingUpdate":{"maxSurge":2}}}}'

# Patch deployment with merge strategy
kubectl patch deployment my-deployment --type merge -p '{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"app","image":"new-image:tag"}]}}}}'

# Patch deployment annotations
kubectl patch deployment my-deployment -p '{"metadata":{"annotations":{"deployment.kubernetes.io/revision":"3"}}}'

# Patch deployment with JSON file
kubectl patch deployment my-deployment --patch-file patch.json

    Django Example

    Patch anihpj Django deployment to modify specific configuration without full replacement.

    # Patch anihpj jobpost deployment replicas
kubectl patch deployment anihpj-jobpost-deployment -p '{"spec":{"replicas":6}}' -n anihpj-services

# Patch anihpj API deployment strategy
kubectl patch deployment anihpj-api-deployment -p '{"spec":{"strategy":{"rollingUpdate":{"maxUnavailable":"0"}}}}' -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-jobpost-deployment patched deployment.apps/anihpj-api-deployment patched
    Example 2: Skills Service Annotation Update

    Patch anihpj Skills service deployment to add monitoring annotations and update container image without full deployment replacement.

    # Patch Skills deployment to add monitoring annotations
kubectl patch deployment anihpj-skills-deployment -p '{"metadata":{"annotations":{"monitoring.anihpj.com/scrape":"true","monitoring.anihpj.com/path":"/metrics"}}}' -n anihpj-services

# Patch Skills deployment container image using merge strategy
kubectl patch deployment anihpj-skills-deployment --type merge -p '{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"skills-container","image":"anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.9.0"}]}}}}' -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-skills-deployment patched deployment.apps/anihpj-skills-deployment patched
    Example 3: Author Service Resource Patching

    Patch anihpj Author service deployment to modify resource requests and limits for optimized performance.

    # Patch Author deployment resource limits using JSON patch
kubectl patch deployment anihpj-author-deployment --type json -p='[{"op":"replace","path":"/spec/template/spec/containers/0/resources/limits/memory","value":"1Gi"}]' -n anihpj-services

# Patch Author deployment to add resource requests
kubectl patch deployment anihpj-author-deployment -p '{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"author-container","resources":{"requests":{"cpu":"200m","memory":"256Mi"}}}]}}}}' -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-author-deployment patched deployment.apps/anihpj-author-deployment patched
    Example 4: Location Service Strategy Configuration

    Patch anihpj Location service deployment to modify rolling update strategy and add environment-specific labels.

    # Patch Location deployment rolling update strategy
kubectl patch deployment anihpj-location-deployment -p '{"spec":{"strategy":{"type":"RollingUpdate","rollingUpdate":{"maxSurge":"2","maxUnavailable":"1"}}}}' -n anihpj-services

# Patch Location deployment to add environment labels
kubectl patch deployment anihpj-location-deployment -p '{"spec":{"template":{"metadata":{"labels":{"environment":"production","version":"v2.1.0"}}}}}' -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-location-deployment patched deployment.apps/anihpj-location-deployment patched
    Example 5: JobPost Service Volume and Secret Patching

    Patch anihpj JobPost service deployment to add volume mounts and update secret references using JSON patch file.

    # Create patch file for JobPost deployment volume configuration
cat > jobpost-volume-patch.json << 'EOF'
{
  "spec": {
    "template": {
      "spec": {
        "volumes": [
          {
            "name": "jobpost-storage",
            "persistentVolumeClaim": {
              "claimName": "jobpost-pvc"
            }
          }
        ],
        "containers": [
          {
            "name": "jobpost-container",
            "volumeMounts": [
              {
                "name": "jobpost-storage",
                "mountPath": "/app/uploads"
              }
            ]
          }
        ]
      }
    }
  }
}
EOF

# Apply patch file to JobPost deployment
kubectl patch deployment anihpj-jobpost-deployment --patch-file jobpost-volume-patch.json -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-jobpost-deployment patched

    Delete Deployment

    Delete a Deployment resource and its associated ReplicaSets and Pods. This operation removes the deployment and all resources it manages.

    HTTP Request

    DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Delete deployment
kubectl delete deployment my-deployment

# Delete deployment with grace period
kubectl delete deployment my-deployment --grace-period=30

# Delete deployment immediately
kubectl delete deployment my-deployment --force --grace-period=0

# Delete deployment from file
kubectl delete -f deployment.yaml

# Delete multiple deployments
kubectl delete deployment deployment1 deployment2 deployment3

    Django Example

    Delete anihpj Django deployment safely with proper cleanup procedures.

    # Delete anihpj staging deployment
kubectl delete deployment anihpj-staging-deployment -n anihpj-staging

# Delete anihpj canary deployment with grace period
kubectl delete deployment anihpj-canary-deployment --grace-period=60 -n anihpj-staging
    deployment.apps "anihpj-staging-deployment" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-canary-deployment" deleted
    Example 2: Development Environment Cleanup

    Delete anihpj development deployments during environment cleanup while preserving data volumes.

    # Delete multiple anihpj development service deployments
kubectl delete deployment anihpj-skills-dev anihpj-author-dev anihpj-location-dev -n anihpj-development

# Delete anihpj jobpost development deployment with confirmation
kubectl delete deployment anihpj-jobpost-dev-deployment -n anihpj-development --wait=true
    deployment.apps "anihpj-skills-dev" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-author-dev" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-location-dev" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-jobpost-dev-deployment" deleted
    Example 3: Force Delete Stuck Deployment

    Force delete anihpj deployment that is stuck in terminating state due to resource conflicts.

    # Attempt graceful deletion of problematic deployment
kubectl delete deployment anihpj-legacy-deployment -n anihpj-services --grace-period=30

# Force delete if graceful deletion fails
kubectl delete deployment anihpj-legacy-deployment -n anihpj-services --force --grace-period=0
    deployment.apps "anihpj-legacy-deployment" deleted
    Example 4: Selective Service Deletion

    Delete specific anihpj service deployments based on labels and environment criteria.

    # Delete anihpj deployments with specific label selector
kubectl delete deployment -l component=api,version=v1.0 -n anihpj-services

# Delete anihpj test environment deployments from YAML files
kubectl delete -f /deployments/anihpj-test-deployments.yaml
    deployment.apps "anihpj-api-v1-deployment" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-skills-test-deployment" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-author-test-deployment" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-location-test-deployment" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-jobpost-test-deployment" deleted
    Example 5: Complete Environment Teardown

    Complete teardown of anihpj staging environment including all service deployments and related resources.

    # Delete all anihpj staging deployments with cascade policy
kubectl delete deployment --all -n anihpj-staging --cascade=foreground

# Verify all deployments are deleted
kubectl get deployments -n anihpj-staging

# Clean up any remaining replica sets
kubectl delete replicaset --all -n anihpj-staging
    deployment.apps "anihpj-web-staging" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-api-staging" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-skills-staging" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-author-staging" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-location-staging" deleted deployment.apps "anihpj-jobpost-staging" deleted No resources found in anihpj-staging namespace. No resources found in anihpj-staging namespace.

    List Deployments

    Retrieve a list of all Deployment resources in a namespace or across all namespaces. This operation returns a DeploymentList object.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments

    kubectl Syntax

    # List deployments in current namespace
kubectl get deployments

# List deployments in all namespaces
kubectl get deployments --all-namespaces

# List deployments with labels
kubectl get deployments -l app=myapp

# List deployments with custom output
kubectl get deployments -o wide

# List deployments with custom columns
kubectl get deployments -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,REPLICAS:.spec.replicas

    Django Example

    List all anihpj Django deployments across different environments and namespaces.

    # List all anihpj deployments
kubectl get deployments -l project=anihpj --all-namespaces

# List anihpj production deployments
kubectl get deployments -l environment=production -n anihpj-production
    NAMESPACE NAME READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE AGE anihpj-services anihpj-web-deployment 3/3 3 3 2d anihpj-services anihpj-api-deployment 5/5 5 5 2d anihpj-staging anihpj-staging-deployment 2/2 2 2 1d NAME READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE AGE anihpj-prod-deployment 8/8 8 8 3d
    Example 2: Service-Specific Deployment Listing

    List anihpj service deployments filtered by component type and display detailed resource information.

    # List anihpj API-related deployments with wide output
kubectl get deployments -l component=api -o wide -n anihpj-services

# List anihpj Skills service deployments with custom columns
kubectl get deployments -l service=skills -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,REPLICAS:.spec.replicas,READY:.status.readyReplicas,IMAGE:.spec.template.spec.containers[0].image --all-namespaces
    NAME READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE AGE CONTAINERS IMAGES SELECTOR anihpj-api-deployment 5/5 5 5 2d api-container anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.5.0 app=anihpj-api anihpj-auth-api-deployment 3/3 3 3 1d auth-container anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.8.0 app=anihpj-auth-api NAME REPLICAS READY IMAGE anihpj-skills-deployment 4 4 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.3.0 anihpj-skills-staging 2 2 anihpj/jobpost-app:v2.3.1-rc
    Example 3: Cross-Environment Deployment Overview

    Get comprehensive overview of anihpj deployments across multiple environments and namespaces with sorting and filtering.

    # List all anihpj deployments sorted by creation timestamp
kubectl get deployments -l project=anihpj --all-namespaces --sort-by=.metadata.creationTimestamp

    Watch Deployments

    Watch for changes to Deployment resources in real-time. This operation establishes a persistent connection to receive updates as deployments are modified.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments?watch=true

    kubectl Syntax

    # Watch deployments for changes
kubectl get deployments --watch

# Watch specific deployment
kubectl get deployment my-deployment --watch

# Watch deployments with output format
kubectl get deployments --watch -o wide

# Watch deployments in all namespaces
kubectl get deployments --all-namespaces --watch

# Watch with custom columns
kubectl get deployments --watch -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,REPLICAS:.spec.replicas

    Django Example

    Watch anihpj Django deployments for real-time monitoring during updates and scaling operations.

    # Watch anihpj web deployment
kubectl get deployment anihpj-web-deployment --watch -n anihpj-services

# Watch all anihpj deployments
kubectl get deployments -l project=anihpj --watch --all-namespaces

    Scale Deployment

    Scale a Deployment by changing the number of replicas. This operation modifies the replica count and triggers the creation or deletion of pods as needed.

    HTTP Request

    PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments/{name}/scale

    kubectl Syntax

    # Scale deployment to specific replica count
kubectl scale deployment my-deployment --replicas=5

# Scale deployment with condition
kubectl scale deployment my-deployment --replicas=3 --current-replicas=5

# Scale multiple deployments
kubectl scale deployment deployment1 deployment2 --replicas=3

# Auto-scale deployment (requires HPA)
kubectl autoscale deployment my-deployment --min=1 --max=10 --cpu-percent=80

# Scale to zero (stop all pods)
kubectl scale deployment my-deployment --replicas=0

    Django Example

    Scale anihpj Django deployments based on traffic and resource requirements.

    # Scale anihpj web deployment for high traffic
kubectl scale deployment anihpj-web-deployment --replicas=8 -n anihpj-services

# Scale down anihpj staging deployment
kubectl scale deployment anihpj-staging-deployment --replicas=1 -n anihpj-staging
    deployment.apps/anihpj-web-deployment scaled deployment.apps/anihpj-staging-deployment scaled
    Example 2: Dynamic Load-Based Scaling

    Scale anihpj service deployments based on traffic patterns and resource utilization metrics.

    # Scale anihpj API deployment for peak traffic hours
kubectl scale deployment anihpj-api-deployment --replicas=12 -n anihpj-services

# Scale anihpj JobPost deployment with conditional scaling
kubectl scale deployment anihpj-jobpost-deployment --replicas=8 --current-replicas=6 -n anihpj-services

# Set up auto-scaling for anihpj Skills deployment
kubectl autoscale deployment anihpj-skills-deployment --min=2 --max=15 --cpu-percent=75 -n anihpj-services
    deployment.apps/anihpj-api-deployment scaled deployment.apps/anihpj-jobpost-deployment scaled horizontalpodautoscaler.autoscaling/anihpj-skills-deployment autoscaled
    Example 3: Multi-Service Coordinated Scaling

    Scale multiple anihpj service deployments simultaneously to maintain proper service ratios and dependencies.

    # Scale multiple anihpj service deployments together
kubectl scale deployment anihpj-skills-deployment anihpj-author-deployment anihpj-location-deployment --replicas=4 -n anihpj-services

# Scale anihpj web deployment to zero for maintenance
kubectl scale deployment anihpj-web-deployment --replicas=0 -n anihpj-services

# Scale anihpj web deployment back up after maintenance
kubectl scale deployment anihpj-web-deployment --replicas=5 -n anihpj-services

    Rollout Management

    Manage Deployment rollouts including checking status, history, pausing, resuming, and rolling back to previous versions.

    kubectl Syntax

    # Check rollout status
kubectl rollout status deployment/my-deployment

# View rollout history
kubectl rollout history deployment/my-deployment

# Pause rollout
kubectl rollout pause deployment/my-deployment

# Resume rollout
kubectl rollout resume deployment/my-deployment

# Rollback to previous version
kubectl rollout undo deployment/my-deployment

# Rollback to specific revision
kubectl rollout undo deployment/my-deployment --to-revision=2

# Restart deployment (rolling restart)
kubectl rollout restart deployment/my-deployment

    Django Example

    Manage anihpj Django deployment rollouts for safe updates and quick rollbacks.

    # Check anihpj API deployment rollout status
kubectl rollout status deployment/anihpj-api-deployment -n anihpj-services

# View anihpj web deployment history
kubectl rollout history deployment/anihpj-web-deployment -n anihpj-services

# Rollback anihpj web deployment
kubectl rollout undo deployment/anihpj-web-deployment -n anihpj-services
    Waiting for deployment "anihpj-api-deployment" rollout to finish: 3 of 5 updated replicas are available... deployment "anihpj-api-deployment" successfully rolled out REVISION CHANGE-CAUSE 1 2 kubectl set image deployment/anihpj-web-deployment web-container=anihpj/web:v2.1.0 3 kubectl set image deployment/anihpj-web-deployment web-container=anihpj/web:v2.2.0 deployment.apps/anihpj-web-deployment rolled back

    StatefulSet

    StatefulSet represents a set of pods with consistent identities, providing stable network identities and persistent storage for stateful applications in Kubernetes. Unlike Deployments, StatefulSets maintain pod ordering and provide guarantees about ordering and uniqueness of pods.

    Key Features

    • Stable Network Identity: Each pod has a persistent hostname based on ordinal index
    • Ordered Deployment: Pods are created, updated, and deleted in order
    • Persistent Storage: Each pod can have its own persistent volume claims
    • Headless Service: Requires a headless service for network identity

    StatefulSet

    StatefulSet represents a set of pods with consistent identities. Identities are defined as stable network identity and persistent storage. The StatefulSet guarantees that a given network identity will always map to the same storage identity.

    API Version & Kind

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet

    Metadata

    metadata (ObjectMeta) - Standard object's metadata including name, namespace, labels, and annotations for the StatefulSet resource.

    Spec

    spec (StatefulSetSpec) - Specification defining the desired identities of pods in this StatefulSet, including replicas, pod template, and volume claim templates.

    Status

    status (StatefulSetStatus) - Current status of pods in this StatefulSet, including replica counts and conditions. This data may be out of date by some window of time.

    StatefulSetSpec

    StatefulSetSpec is the specification of a StatefulSet, defining how pods should be created and managed with consistent identities.

    Required Fields

    serviceName (string)

    serviceName is the name of the service that governs this StatefulSet. This service must exist before the StatefulSet and is responsible for the network identity of the set. Pods get DNS/hostnames following the pattern: pod-specific-string.serviceName.default.svc.cluster.local

    selector (LabelSelector)

    selector is a label query over pods that should match the replica count. It must match the pod template's labels. Used to identify which pods belong to this StatefulSet.

    template (PodTemplateSpec)

    template describes the pod that will be created if insufficient replicas are detected. Each pod stamped out by the StatefulSet will fulfill this template but have a unique identity. Pod naming follows the format <statefulsetname>-<podindex>. Only allowed template.spec.restartPolicy value is "Always".

    Optional Fields

    replicas (int32)

    replicas is the desired number of replicas of the given template. These are replicas with consistent identity. If unspecified, defaults to 1.

    updateStrategy (StatefulSetUpdateStrategy)

    updateStrategy indicates the strategy that will be employed to update pods in the StatefulSet when a revision is made to the template.

    • updateStrategy.type - Type of update strategy. Default is RollingUpdate
    • updateStrategy.rollingUpdate.maxUnavailable - Maximum number of pods unavailable during update
    • updateStrategy.rollingUpdate.partition - Ordinal at which the StatefulSet should be partitioned for updates
    podManagementPolicy (string)

    podManagementPolicy controls how pods are created during initial scale up, replacement, or scaling down. Options:

    • OrderedReady (default) - Pods created in increasing order, controller waits until each pod is ready
    • Parallel - Pods created in parallel without waiting, deleted all at once on scale down
    volumeClaimTemplates ([]PersistentVolumeClaim)

    volumeClaimTemplates is a list of claims that pods are allowed to reference. The StatefulSet controller maps network identities to claims maintaining pod identity. Every claim must have at least one matching volumeMount in the pod template.

    revisionHistoryLimit (int32)

    revisionHistoryLimit is the maximum number of revisions maintained in StatefulSet's revision history. Default value is 10.

    minReadySeconds (int32)

    minReadySeconds - Minimum number of seconds for which a newly created pod should be ready without container crashes for it to be considered available. Defaults to 0.

    persistentVolumeClaimRetentionPolicy

    persistentVolumeClaimRetentionPolicy describes the lifecycle of persistent volume claims created from volumeClaimTemplates:

    • whenDeleted - What happens to PVCs when StatefulSet is deleted (Retain/Delete)
    • whenScaled - What happens to PVCs when StatefulSet is scaled down (Retain/Delete)

    StatefulSetStatus

    StatefulSetStatus represents the current state of a StatefulSet, providing information about replica counts and conditions.

    Status Fields

    replicas (int32)

    replicas is the number of pods created by the StatefulSet controller.

    readyReplicas (int32)

    readyReplicas is the number of pods created for this StatefulSet with a Ready condition.

    currentReplicas (int32)

    currentReplicas is the number of pods created by the StatefulSet controller from the StatefulSet version indicated by currentRevision.

    updatedReplicas (int32)

    updatedReplicas is the number of pods created by the StatefulSet controller from the StatefulSet version indicated by updateRevision.

    availableReplicas (int32)

    availableReplicas is the total number of available pods (ready for at least minReadySeconds) targeted by this StatefulSet.

    conditions ([]StatefulSetCondition)

    conditions represents the latest available observations of a StatefulSet's current state.

    currentRevision (string)

    currentRevision indicates the version of the StatefulSet used to generate pods in the sequence [0,currentReplicas).

    updateRevision (string)

    updateRevision indicates the version of the StatefulSet used to generate pods in the sequence [replicas-updatedReplicas,replicas).

    observedGeneration (int64)

    observedGeneration is the most recent generation observed for this StatefulSet. It corresponds to the StatefulSet's generation updated by the API Server.

    StatefulSetList

    StatefulSetList is a collection of StatefulSets used when retrieving multiple StatefulSet resources.

    API Structure

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSetList
metadata: ListMeta
items: []StatefulSet

    Fields

    metadata (ListMeta)

    metadata - Standard list's metadata containing information about the list of StatefulSets.

    items ([]StatefulSet)

    items is the list of StatefulSet objects contained in this StatefulSetList.

    StatefulSet Operations

    StatefulSet operations provide comprehensive management of stateful workloads through the Kubernetes API. These operations allow you to create, read, update, delete, and monitor StatefulSets for applications requiring persistent storage and stable network identities.

    Create StatefulSet

    Create a new StatefulSet resource in a namespace. This operation deploys a stateful application with ordered pod creation and persistent storage.

    HTTP Request

    POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/statefulsets

    kubectl Syntax

    # Create StatefulSet from YAML file
kubectl create -f statefulset.yaml

# Create StatefulSet from YAML with custom namespace
kubectl create -f statefulset.yaml -n my-namespace

# Create StatefulSet with dry-run
kubectl create -f statefulset.yaml --dry-run=client

# Apply StatefulSet configuration
kubectl apply -f statefulset.yaml

# Create StatefulSet with field manager
kubectl apply -f statefulset.yaml --field-manager=kubectl

    Django Example

    Create anihpj Django StatefulSet for database services requiring persistent storage and stable network identities.

    # Create anihpj PostgreSQL StatefulSet for persistent database
kubectl apply -f anihpj-postgres-statefulset.yaml -n anihpj-services

# Create anihpj Redis StatefulSet for session storage
kubectl apply -f anihpj-redis-statefulset.yaml -n anihpj-services
    statefulset.apps/anihpj-postgres-statefulset created statefulset.apps/anihpj-redis-statefulset created
    Example 2: Skills Service Database StatefulSet

    Create anihpj Skills service dedicated PostgreSQL StatefulSet with persistent volume claims for skills data storage.

    # Create Skills service PostgreSQL StatefulSet
cat << 'EOF' | kubectl apply -f - -n anihpj-services
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-postgres
  labels:
    app: anihpj-skills-db
    service: skills
spec:
  serviceName: anihpj-skills-postgres-service
  replicas: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-skills-db
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-skills-db
        service: skills
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: postgres
        image: postgres:15
        env:
        - name: POSTGRES_DB
          value: "anihpj_skills"
        - name: POSTGRES_USER
          value: "anihpj_user"
        - name: POSTGRES_PASSWORD
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-skills-db-secret
              key: password
        volumeMounts:
        - name: postgres-storage
          mountPath: /var/lib/postgresql/data
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: postgres-storage
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 5Gi
EOF
    statefulset.apps/anihpj-skills-postgres created
    Example 3: Author Service Elasticsearch StatefulSet

    Create anihpj Author service Elasticsearch StatefulSet cluster for author search indexing with persistent storage.

    # Create Author service Elasticsearch StatefulSet cluster
kubectl apply -f - << 'EOF'
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-author-elasticsearch
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-author-search
    service: author
spec:
  serviceName: anihpj-author-elasticsearch-service
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-author-search
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-author-search
        service: author
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: elasticsearch
        image: elasticsearch:8.9.0
        env:
        - name: cluster.name
          value: "anihpj-author-cluster"
        - name: node.name
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.name
        - name: discovery.seed_hosts
          value: "anihpj-author-elasticsearch-0,anihpj-author-elasticsearch-1,anihpj-author-elasticsearch-2"
        - name: cluster.initial_master_nodes
          value: "anihpj-author-elasticsearch-0,anihpj-author-elasticsearch-1,anihpj-author-elasticsearch-2"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: elasticsearch-storage
          mountPath: /usr/share/elasticsearch/data
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: elasticsearch-storage
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 10Gi
EOF
    statefulset.apps/anihpj-author-elasticsearch created
    Example 4: Location Service MongoDB StatefulSet

    Create anihpj Location service MongoDB StatefulSet with replica set configuration for geographic data storage.

    # Create Location service MongoDB StatefulSet
kubectl create -f - << 'EOF'
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-location-mongodb
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-location-db
    service: location
spec:
  serviceName: anihpj-location-mongodb-service
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-location-db
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-location-db
        service: location
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: mongodb
        image: mongo:6.0
        env:
        - name: MONGO_INITDB_ROOT_USERNAME
          value: "anihpj_location_admin"
        - name: MONGO_INITDB_ROOT_PASSWORD
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-location-mongodb-secret
              key: password
        - name: MONGO_INITDB_DATABASE
          value: "anihpj_locations"
        command:
        - mongod
        - --replSet
        - anihpj-location-rs
        - --bind_ip_all
        volumeMounts:
        - name: mongodb-storage
          mountPath: /data/db
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: mongodb-storage
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 8Gi

    Example 5: JobPost Service ClickHouse StatefulSet

    Create anihpj JobPost service ClickHouse StatefulSet for analytics and job posting metrics with persistent storage and clustering.

    # Create JobPost service ClickHouse StatefulSet for analytics
kubectl apply -n anihpj-services -f - << 'EOF'
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse
  labels:
    app: anihpj-jobpost-analytics
    service: jobpost
spec:
  serviceName: anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-service
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-jobpost-analytics
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost-analytics
        service: jobpost
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: clickhouse
        image: clickhouse/clickhouse-server:23.8
        env:
        - name: CLICKHOUSE_DB
          value: "anihpj_jobpost_analytics"
        - name: CLICKHOUSE_USER
          value: "anihpj_analytics_user"
        - name: CLICKHOUSE_PASSWORD
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-secret
              key: password
        - name: CLICKHOUSE_DEFAULT_ACCESS_MANAGEMENT
          value: "1"
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8123
          name: http
        - containerPort: 9000
          name: native
        volumeMounts:
        - name: clickhouse-storage
          mountPath: /var/lib/clickhouse
        - name: clickhouse-logs
          mountPath: /var/log/clickhouse-server
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: clickhouse-storage
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 20Gi
  - metadata:
      name: clickhouse-logs
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]  
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 2Gi
EOF
    statefulset.apps/anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse created

    Get StatefulSet

    Read the specified StatefulSet resource to retrieve its current configuration and status information.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/statefulsets/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Get specific StatefulSet
kubectl get statefulset my-statefulset

# Get StatefulSet with detailed output
kubectl get statefulset my-statefulset -o wide

# Get StatefulSet in YAML format
kubectl get statefulset my-statefulset -o yaml

# Get StatefulSet in JSON format
kubectl get statefulset my-statefulset -o json

# Describe StatefulSet for detailed information
kubectl describe statefulset my-statefulset

    Update StatefulSet

    Replace the specified StatefulSet resource with a new configuration. This operation allows you to modify StatefulSet specifications including pod templates, replicas, and update strategies.

    HTTP Request

    PUT /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/statefulsets/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Update StatefulSet from file
kubectl replace -f statefulset.yaml

# Update StatefulSet image
kubectl set image statefulset/my-statefulset container-name=new-image:tag

# Update StatefulSet replicas
kubectl scale statefulset my-statefulset --replicas=5

# Apply updated StatefulSet configuration
kubectl apply -f updated-statefulset.yaml

# Update StatefulSet with patch
kubectl patch statefulset my-statefulset -p '{"spec":{"replicas":3}}'

    Django Example

    Update anihpj Django StatefulSet configurations for database services to handle increased load and new requirements.

    # Update anihpj PostgreSQL StatefulSet image version
kubectl set image statefulset/anihpj-postgres-statefulset postgres=postgres:16 -n anihpj-services

# Scale anihpj Redis StatefulSet replicas
kubectl scale statefulset anihpj-redis-statefulset --replicas=3 -n anihpj-services
    statefulset.apps/anihpj-postgres-statefulset image updated statefulset.apps/anihpj-redis-statefulset scaled

    Update anihpj Skills service PostgreSQL StatefulSet with enhanced configuration for better performance and resource allocation.

    # Update Skills PostgreSQL StatefulSet with new resource limits

    Patch StatefulSet

    Partially update a StatefulSet resource by modifying specific fields without replacing the entire resource definition. This operation allows targeted updates to StatefulSet configuration.

    HTTP Request

    PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/statefulsets/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Patch StatefulSet replicas
kubectl patch statefulset my-statefulset -p '{"spec":{"replicas":5}}'

# Patch StatefulSet with JSON file
kubectl patch statefulset my-statefulset --patch-file patch.json

# Patch StatefulSet with merge strategy
kubectl patch statefulset my-statefulset --type merge -p '{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"app","image":"new-image:tag"}]}}}}'

# Patch StatefulSet annotations
kubectl patch statefulset my-statefulset -p '{"metadata":{"annotations":{"deployment.kubernetes.io/revision":"3"}}}'

# Patch StatefulSet update strategy
kubectl patch statefulset my-statefulset -p '{"spec":{"updateStrategy":{"type":"RollingUpdate","rollingUpdate":{"partition":2}}}}'

    Django Example

    Patch anihpj Django StatefulSet to modify specific configuration without full replacement for database services.

    # Patch anihpj PostgreSQL StatefulSet replicas
kubectl patch statefulset anihpj-postgres-statefulset -p '{"spec":{"replicas":2}}' -n anihpj-services

# Patch anihpj Redis StatefulSet update strategy
kubectl patch statefulset anihpj-redis-statefulset -p '{"spec":{"updateStrategy":{"rollingUpdate":{"partition":1}}}}' -n anihpj-services
    statefulset.apps/anihpj-postgres-statefulset patched statefulset.apps/anihpj-redis-statefulset patched
    Example 2: Skills Service Database Resource Updates

    Patch anihpj Skills service PostgreSQL StatefulSet to update resource limits and environment variables for optimal performance.

    # Patch Skills PostgreSQL StatefulSet resource limits
kubectl patch statefulset anihpj-skills-postgres -n anihpj-services --type='merge' -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"postgres","resources":{"limits":{"memory":"4Gi","cpu":"2000m"},"requests":{"memory":"2Gi","cpu":"1000m"}}}]}}}}'

# Patch Skills PostgreSQL with new environment variables for performance tuning
kubectl patch statefulset anihpj-skills-postgres -n anihpj-services -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"postgres","env":[{"name":"POSTGRES_SHARED_BUFFERS","value":"512MB"},{"name":"POSTGRES_EFFECTIVE_CACHE_SIZE","value":"2GB"},{"name":"POSTGRES_WORK_MEM","value":"16MB"}]}]}}}}'
    statefulset.apps/anihpj-skills-postgres patched statefulset.apps/anihpj-skills-postgres patched
    Example 3: Author Service Elasticsearch Configuration Tuning

    Patch anihpj Author service Elasticsearch StatefulSet to optimize cluster configuration and memory settings for better search performance.

    # Patch Author Elasticsearch StatefulSet with memory optimization

    Patch anihpj Location service MongoDB StatefulSet to enhance replica set configuration and add geographic indexing optimizations.

    # Patch Location MongoDB StatefulSet with enhanced configuration
kubectl patch statefulset anihpj-location-mongodb -n anihpj-services --type='merge' -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"mongodb","env":[{"name":"MONGO_OPLOG_SIZE","value":"1024"},{"name":"MONGO_GEO_INDEXING","value":"enabled"},{"name":"MONGO_TEXT_SEARCH","value":"enabled"}]}]}}}}'

# Patch MongoDB StatefulSet to update readiness probe for better reliability
kubectl patch statefulset anihpj-location-mongodb -n anihpj-services -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"mongodb","readinessProbe":{"exec":{"command":["mongo","--eval","db.adminCommand('\''ping'\'')"]},"initialDelaySeconds":30,"periodSeconds":10}}]}}}}'
    statefulset.apps/anihpj-location-mongodb patched statefulset.apps/anihpj-location-mongodb patched
    Example 5: JobPost Service ClickHouse Analytics Enhancement

    Patch anihpj JobPost service ClickHouse StatefulSet to optimize analytics performance and add advanced configuration for data processing.

    # Create patch file for JobPost ClickHouse optimization
cat > jobpost-clickhouse-patch.json << 'EOF'
{
  "spec": {
    "template": {
      "spec": {
        "containers": [
          {
            "name": "clickhouse",
            "env": [
              {
                "name": "CLICKHOUSE_MAX_MEMORY_USAGE",
                "value": "8000000000"
              },
              {
                "name": "CLICKHOUSE_MAX_THREADS",
                "value": "8"
              },
              {
                "name": "CLICKHOUSE_BACKGROUND_POOL_SIZE",
                "value": "16"
              },
              {
                "name": "CLICKHOUSE_MERGE_TREE_MAX_ROWS_TO_USE_CACHE",
                "value": "1000000"
              }
            ],
            "resources": {
              "limits": {
                "memory": "8Gi",
                "cpu": "4000m"
              },
              "requests": {
                "memory": "4Gi", 
                "cpu": "2000m"
              }
            }
          }
        ]
      }
    }
  }
}
EOF

# Apply patch file to JobPost ClickHouse StatefulSet
kubectl patch statefulset anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse --patch-file jobpost-clickhouse-patch.json -n anihpj-services
    statefulset.apps/anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse patched

    Delete StatefulSet

    Delete a StatefulSet resource and optionally its associated pods and persistent volume claims. This operation removes the StatefulSet but can preserve or delete persistent storage based on configuration.

    HTTP Request

    DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/statefulsets/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Delete StatefulSet
kubectl delete statefulset my-statefulset

# Delete StatefulSet and pods immediately
kubectl delete statefulset my-statefulset --cascade=foreground

# Delete StatefulSet but keep pods
kubectl delete statefulset my-statefulset --cascade=orphan

# Delete StatefulSet from file
kubectl delete -f statefulset.yaml

# Delete StatefulSet with grace period
kubectl delete statefulset my-statefulset --grace-period=30

    Django Example

    Delete anihpj Django StatefulSet resources safely while considering data persistence requirements.

    # Delete anihpj Redis StatefulSet (cache data can be lost)
kubectl delete statefulset anihpj-redis-statefulset -n anihpj-services

# Delete anihpj test PostgreSQL StatefulSet with immediate cleanup
kubectl delete statefulset anihpj-test-postgres --cascade=foreground -n anihpj-testing

    ControllerRevision

    ControllerRevision Overview

    ControllerRevision - Immutable snapshot of state data
    ControllerRevisionList - Collection of controller revisions
    Operations - API operations for management
    Official Docs: ControllerRevision v1 API | API Version: apps/v1

    ControllerRevision implements an immutable snapshot of state data. Used by DaemonSet and StatefulSet controllers for update and rollback operations.

    Description

    ControllerRevision implements an immutable snapshot of state data. Clients are responsible for serializing and deserializing the objects that contain their internal state. Once a ControllerRevision has been successfully created, it cannot be updated. The API Server will fail validation of all requests that attempt to mutate the Data field. ControllerRevisions may, however, be deleted. Note that, due to its use by both the DaemonSet and StatefulSet controllers for update and rollback, this object is beta. However, it may be subject to name and representation changes in future releases, and clients should not depend on its stability. It is primarily for internal use by controllers.

    Syntax

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevision
metadata:
  name: controller-revision-name
  namespace: namespace-name
revision: 1
data:
  # RawExtension - serialized representation of the state

    Parameters

    apiVersion (string): API version, always "apps/v1"
    kind (string): Resource type, always "ControllerRevision"
    metadata (ObjectMeta): Standard object metadata containing name, namespace, labels, and annotations
    revision (int64, required): Revision indicates the revision of the state represented by Data
    data (RawExtension): Data is the serialized representation of the state

    Return Value

    Returns a ControllerRevision object representing an immutable snapshot of controller state data with revision tracking for rollback operations.

    Examples

    Example 1: Skills Service DaemonSet Revision

    View ControllerRevision for anihpj Skills service DaemonSet to track configuration changes and enable rollback functionality.

    # Get ControllerRevisions for Skills DaemonSet
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n anihpj-services -l controller.kubernetes.io/name=anihpj-skills-daemonset

# View specific ControllerRevision details
kubectl describe controllerrevision anihpj-skills-daemonset-7b9f8d6c45 -n anihpj-services
    NAME CONTROLLER REVISION AGE anihpj-skills-daemonset-7b9f8d6c45 anihpj-skills-daemonset 1 2d anihpj-skills-daemonset-9c4e2f8a67 anihpj-skills-daemonset 2 1d
    Example 2: Author Service StatefulSet Revision History

    Examine ControllerRevision history for anihpj Author service StatefulSet to understand deployment evolution and rollback points.

    # List all ControllerRevisions for Author StatefulSet
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n anihpj-services --selector=controller.kubernetes.io/name=anihpj-author-elasticsearch

# Get detailed revision information
kubectl get controllerrevision anihpj-author-elasticsearch-5f8c9d7e23 -n anihpj-services -o yaml
    NAME CONTROLLER REVISION AGE anihpj-author-elasticsearch-5f8c9d7e23 anihpj-author-elasticsearch 1 3d anihpj-author-elasticsearch-7a1b4e9f56 anihpj-author-elasticsearch 2 2d anihpj-author-elasticsearch-8c2d5f1a89 anihpj-author-elasticsearch 3 1d
    Example 3: Location Service MongoDB StatefulSet Revision Comparison

    Compare ControllerRevisions for anihpj Location service MongoDB StatefulSet to identify configuration differences between versions.

    # Get revision details for comparison
kubectl get controllerrevision anihpj-location-mongodb-6d4a8b9c12 -n anihpj-services -o json | jq .data

# List revisions with creation timestamps

    Manage ControllerRevisions for anihpj JobPost service ClickHouse StatefulSet including cleanup of old revisions to maintain history.

    ControllerRevisionList

    ControllerRevisionList is a resource containing a list of ControllerRevision objects.

    Description

    ControllerRevisionList is a resource containing a list of ControllerRevision objects. It provides a way to list and manage multiple controller revisions as a collection, useful for batch operations and comprehensive revision management.

    Syntax

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevisionList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: "string"
items:
  - # Array of ControllerRevision objects

    Parameters

    apiVersion (string): API version, always "apps/v1"
    kind (string): Resource type, always "ControllerRevisionList"
    metadata (ListMeta): Standard list metadata
    items ([]ControllerRevision, required): Items is the list of ControllerRevision objects

    Return Value

    Returns a ControllerRevisionList object containing an array of ControllerRevision objects matching the specified criteria.

    Examples

    Example 1: Skills Service Revision List

    List all ControllerRevisions for anihpj Skills service to review deployment history and available rollback points.

    # Get ControllerRevisionList for Skills service
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n anihpj-services -l app=anihpj-skills -o yaml
    apiVersion: v1 kind: List items: - apiVersion: apps/v1 kind: ControllerRevision metadata: name: anihpj-skills-daemonset-7b9f8d6c45 namespace: anihpj-services
    Example 2: Author Service Elasticsearch Revision History

    Example 3: Location Service MongoDB Revision Collection

    ControllerRevision Operations

    Read ControllerRevision

    Read the specified ControllerRevision resource to retrieve detailed information about a specific revision snapshot.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Get specific ControllerRevision
kubectl get controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace

# Get ControllerRevision with output formatting
kubectl get controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace -o yaml

# Get ControllerRevision details
kubectl describe controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace

# Get ControllerRevision with custom columns
kubectl get controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,REVISION:.revision

# Get ControllerRevision with JSON path
kubectl get controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace -o jsonpath='{.revision}'

    List ControllerRevision

    List or watch ControllerRevision objects in a specific namespace to monitor revision history and track deployment changes.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions

    kubectl Syntax

    # List all ControllerRevisions in namespace
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n my-namespace

# List with labels
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n my-namespace -l app=my-app

# List with field selector
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n my-namespace --field-selector metadata.name=my-revision

# Watch ControllerRevisions
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n my-namespace -w

# List with custom output
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n my-namespace -o wide

    Django Example

    List anihpj Django ControllerRevisions to monitor revision history across all services for deployment tracking.

    # List all ControllerRevisions in anihpj services namespace
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n anihpj-services

    List All Namespaces ControllerRevision

    List or watch ControllerRevision objects across all namespaces to provide cluster-wide revision monitoring and management.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/controllerrevisions

    kubectl Syntax

    # List ControllerRevisions across all namespaces
kubectl get controllerrevisions --all-namespaces

# List with specific labels across all namespaces
kubectl get controllerrevisions --all-namespaces -l app=my-app

# Watch ControllerRevisions across all namespaces
kubectl get controllerrevisions --all-namespaces -w

# List with custom output format
kubectl get controllerrevisions --all-namespaces -o wide

# List with field selector
kubectl get controllerrevisions --all-namespaces --field-selector metadata.namespace=production

    Django Example
