    Create ControllerRevision

    Create a new ControllerRevision resource to capture an immutable snapshot of controller state data for rollback and versioning purposes.

    HTTP Request

    POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions

    kubectl Syntax

    # Create ControllerRevision from YAML file
kubectl apply -f controller-revision.yaml

# Create ControllerRevision with inline definition
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevision
metadata:
  name: my-revision
  namespace: my-namespace
revision: 1
data:
  # serialized controller state
EOF

# Create with dry run
kubectl apply -f controller-revision.yaml --dry-run=client

# Create with field manager
kubectl apply -f controller-revision.yaml --field-manager=my-manager

# Create and validate
kubectl apply -f controller-revision.yaml --validate=true

    Django Example

    Create anihpj Django ControllerRevision to manually capture configuration snapshots for critical deployment states.

    # Create Skills service ControllerRevision manually
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevision
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-manual-snapshot-v1
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-skills
    revision-type: manual
revision: 10
data:
  # Manual snapshot of Skills DaemonSet configuration
EOF

# Create Author Elasticsearch ControllerRevision with backup
kubectl apply -f anihpj-author-elasticsearch-revision.yaml -n anihpj-services
    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-skills-manual-snapshot-v1 created controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-author-elasticsearch-backup-v3 created
    Example 2: Location Service MongoDB Revision Creation

    Create anihpj Location service MongoDB ControllerRevision to preserve critical database configuration states for disaster recovery.

    # Create Location MongoDB ControllerRevision with backup configuration
cat > anihpj-location-mongodb-revision.yaml << 'EOF'
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevision
metadata:
  name: anihpj-location-mongodb-backup-v4
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-location-mongodb
    backup-type: critical-state
    created-by: admin
revision: 4
data:
  # Serialized MongoDB StatefulSet configuration
  # with geographic indexing and replication settings
EOF

kubectl apply -f anihpj-location-mongodb-revision.yaml
    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-location-mongodb-backup-v4 created
    Example 3: JobPost Service ClickHouse Revision Backup

    Create anihpj JobPost service ClickHouse ControllerRevision to backup analytics database configuration before major performance tuning.

    # Create JobPost ClickHouse pre-optimization ControllerRevision
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevision
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-pre-optimization
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse
    snapshot-reason: pre-performance-tuning
    optimization-phase: baseline

  # Pre-optimization ClickHouse StatefulSet configuration
  # baseline performance settings
EOF
    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-pre-optimization created
    Example 4: Multi-Service Revision Synchronization

    Create synchronized anihpj ControllerRevisions across Skills, Author, Location, and JobPost services for coordinated deployment snapshots.

    # Create synchronized revisions for all services
for service in skills author location jobpost; do
  kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevision
metadata:
  name: anihpj-$service-sync-snapshot-v6
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-$service
    sync-group: release-v2.1.0
    coordination: synchronized
revision: 6
data:
  # Synchronized $service configuration
EOF
done
    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-skills-sync-snapshot-v6 created controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-author-sync-snapshot-v6 created controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-location-sync-snapshot-v6 created controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-jobpost-sync-snapshot-v6 created
    Example 5: Emergency Rollback Revision Creation

    Create emergency anihpj ControllerRevisions to capture known-good states before critical system updates and migrations.

    # Create emergency rollback revisions
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevision
metadata:
  name: anihpj-emergency-rollback-point
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    emergency: "true"
    rollback-point: stable-v2.0.5
    criticality: high
revision: 999
data:
  # Emergency rollback configuration
  # stable anihpj platform state
EOF
    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-emergency-rollback-point created

    Update ControllerRevision

    Replace the specified ControllerRevision resource. Note: ControllerRevisions are typically immutable, so updates are generally not allowed for the data field.

    HTTP Request

    PUT /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Update ControllerRevision from YAML file
kubectl apply -f controller-revision-updated.yaml

# Replace ControllerRevision completely
kubectl replace -f controller-revision.yaml

# Update with force
kubectl replace -f controller-revision.yaml --force

# Update with cascade deletion
kubectl replace -f controller-revision.yaml --cascade=foreground

# Update with dry run
kubectl apply -f controller-revision.yaml --dry-run=client

    Django Example

    Update anihpj Django ControllerRevision metadata such as labels and annotations while preserving immutable data field.

    # Update Skills ControllerRevision labels only
kubectl patch controllerrevision anihpj-skills-daemonset-7b9f8d6c45 -n anihpj-services --type='merge' -p='{"metadata":{"labels":{"updated":"true","maintenance":"completed"}}}'

# Update Author ControllerRevision annotations
kubectl annotate controllerrevision anihpj-author-elasticsearch-8c2d5f1a89 -n anihpj-services deployment.status="verified"
    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-skills-daemonset-7b9f8d6c45 patched controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-author-elasticsearch-8c2d5f1a89 annotated
    Example 2: Location Service MongoDB Revision Metadata Update

    Update anihpj Location service MongoDB ControllerRevision metadata to add operational tracking and maintenance information.

    # Update Location MongoDB ControllerRevision with maintenance info
kubectl patch controllerrevision anihpj-location-mongodb-9e3b7d6f28 -n anihpj-services --type='merge' -p='{"metadata":{"annotations":{"maintenance.window":"2024-09-08T02:00:00Z","verified.by":"ops-team","rollback.tested":"true"}}}'

# Add operational labels
kubectl label controllerrevision anihpj-location-mongodb-9e3b7d6f28 -n anihpj-services environment=production stability=verified
    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-location-mongodb-9e3b7d6f28 patched controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-location-mongodb-9e3b7d6f28 labeled

    Update anihpj JobPost service ClickHouse ControllerRevision with performance metrics and optimization tracking annotations.

    Update anihpj ControllerRevisions across Skills, Author, Location, and JobPost services with coordinated release labeling.

    # Add release labels to all service revisions

    Example 5: Emergency Revision Status Update

    Update anihpj emergency ControllerRevision with incident response tracking and resolution status annotations.

    # Update emergency revision with incident tracking
kubectl annotate controllerrevision anihpj-emergency-rollback-point -n anihpj-services \
  incident.id="INC-2024-0908-001" \

    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-emergency-rollback-point annotated controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-emergency-rollback-point labeled

    Patch ControllerRevision

    Partially update the specified ControllerRevision resource by modifying specific fields without replacing the entire resource definition. Typically used for metadata updates.

    HTTP Request

    PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Patch ControllerRevision with JSON
kubectl patch controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace -p '{"metadata":{"labels":{"updated":"true"}}}'

# Patch with YAML
kubectl patch controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace --type merge -p 'metadata: labels: environment: production'

# Patch with JSON file
kubectl patch controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace --patch-file patch.json

# Patch with strategic merge
kubectl patch controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace --type strategic -p '{"metadata":{"annotations":{"note":"updated"}}}'

# Patch with JSON merge
kubectl patch controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace --type merge -p '{"metadata":{"finalizers":["custom-finalizer"]}}'

    Django Example

    Patch anihpj Django ControllerRevision to add operational metadata and tracking information without modifying immutable data.

    # Patch Skills ControllerRevision with deployment tracking
kubectl patch controllerrevision anihpj-skills-daemonset-7b9f8d6c45 -n anihpj-services --type='merge' -p='{"metadata":{"labels":{"deployment.phase":"completed","verification.status":"passed"}}}'

# Patch Author ControllerRevision with performance annotations
kubectl patch controllerrevision anihpj-author-elasticsearch-8c2d5f1a89 -n anihpj-services -p='{"metadata":{"annotations":{"performance.baseline":"established","load.tested":"true"}}}'
    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-skills-daemonset-7b9f8d6c45 patched controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-author-elasticsearch-8c2d5f1a89 patched
    Example 2: Location Service MongoDB Revision Operational Patch

    Patch anihpj Location service MongoDB ControllerRevision with geographic indexing verification and operational readiness status.

    # Patch Location MongoDB ControllerRevision with geo-indexing status
kubectl patch controllerrevision anihpj-location-mongodb-9e3b7d6f28 -n anihpj-services --type='json' -p='[{"op": "add", "path": "/metadata/annotations/geo-indexing.verified", "value": "true"}, {"op": "add", "path": "/metadata/annotations/replication.status", "value": "healthy"}]'

# Patch with operational readiness
kubectl patch controllerrevision anihpj-location-mongodb-9e3b7d6f28 -n anihpj-services -p='{"metadata":{"labels":{"operational.ready":"true","backup.verified":"true"}}}'
    controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-location-mongodb-9e3b7d6f28 patched controllerrevision.apps/anihpj-location-mongodb-9e3b7d6f28 patched

    Delete ControllerRevision

    Delete the specified ControllerRevision resource to remove outdated revision snapshots and clean up revision history.

    HTTP Request

    DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Delete specific ControllerRevision
kubectl delete controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace

# Delete with grace period
kubectl delete controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace --grace-period=30

# Delete immediately
kubectl delete controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace --grace-period=0 --force

# Delete with cascade
kubectl delete controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace --cascade=foreground

# Delete with dry run
kubectl delete controllerrevision my-revision -n my-namespace --dry-run=client

    Django Example

    Delete outdated anihpj Django ControllerRevisions to maintain clean revision history and optimize storage usage.

    # Delete old Skills ControllerRevision
kubectl delete controllerrevision anihpj-skills-daemonset-5a6b7c8d94 -n anihpj-services

# Delete obsolete Author ControllerRevision
kubectl delete controllerrevision anihpj-author-elasticsearch-5f8c9d7e23 -n anihpj-services
    controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-skills-daemonset-5a6b7c8d94" deleted controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-author-elasticsearch-5f8c9d7e23" deleted
    Example 2: Location Service MongoDB Revision Cleanup

    Delete anihpj Location service MongoDB ControllerRevisions that are no longer needed for rollback to maintain optimal revision history.

    # Delete outdated Location MongoDB ControllerRevisions
kubectl delete controllerrevision anihpj-location-mongodb-6d4a8b9c12 -n anihpj-services

# Delete with confirmation
kubectl delete controllerrevision anihpj-location-mongodb-8f2c1e5a47 -n anihpj-services --wait=true
    controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-location-mongodb-6d4a8b9c12" deleted controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-location-mongodb-8f2c1e5a47" deleted
    Example 3: JobPost Service ClickHouse Revision Archive

    Delete anihpj JobPost service ClickHouse ControllerRevisions after archiving to external storage for compliance and space management.

    # Archive and delete old JobPost ClickHouse ControllerRevisions
kubectl get controllerrevision anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-4a7c8e1b93 -n anihpj-services -o yaml > archive/anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-4a7c8e1b93.yaml
kubectl delete controllerrevision anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-4a7c8e1b93 -n anihpj-services

# Delete with backup verification
kubectl delete controllerrevision anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-7d5f2a9c46 -n anihpj-services --wait=true
    controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-4a7c8e1b93" deleted controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-jobpost-clickhouse-7d5f2a9c46" deleted
    Example 4: Automated Revision Retention Policy

    Delete anihpj ControllerRevisions based on retention policy to maintain only the last 3 revisions per service for optimal management.

    # Delete old revisions keeping only last 3 per service
for service in skills author location jobpost; do
  # Get revisions sorted by creation time (oldest first)
  old_revisions=$(kubectl get controllerrevisions -n anihpj-services -l app=anihpj-$service --sort-by=.metadata.creationTimestamp -o name | head -n -3)
  if [ ! -z "$old_revisions" ]; then
    echo "$old_revisions" | xargs kubectl delete -n anihpj-services
  fi
done
    controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-skills-daemonset-1a2b3c4d56" deleted controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-author-elasticsearch-2b3c4d5e67" deleted controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-location-mongodb-3c4d5e6f78" deleted
    Example 5: Emergency Revision Cleanup

    Delete anihpj emergency ControllerRevisions after incident resolution to clean up crisis management artifacts and maintain system hygiene.

    # Delete emergency revisions after incident resolution
kubectl delete controllerrevision anihpj-emergency-rollback-point -n anihpj-services

# Delete test revisions used during incident
kubectl delete controllerrevisions -n anihpj-services -l emergency=true,incident.resolved=true

# Verify cleanup
kubectl get controllerrevisions -n anihpj-services -l emergency=true
    controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-emergency-rollback-point" deleted controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-emergency-test-revision-1" deleted controllerrevision.apps "anihpj-emergency-test-revision-2" deleted No resources found in anihpj-services namespace.

    Delete Collection ControllerRevision

    Delete collection of ControllerRevision resources based on label selectors or field selectors to perform bulk cleanup operations.

    HTTP Request

    DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions

    kubectl Syntax

    # Delete ControllerRevisions by label selector
kubectl delete controllerrevisions -n my-namespace -l app=my-app

# Delete with field selector
kubectl delete controllerrevisions -n my-namespace --field-selector metadata.name=my-revision

# Delete all ControllerRevisions in namespace
kubectl delete controllerrevisions -n my-namespace --all

# Delete with grace period
kubectl delete controllerrevisions -n my-namespace -l version=old --grace-period=30

# Delete with dry run
kubectl delete controllerrevisions -n my-namespace -l app=my-app --dry-run=client

    Django Example

    Delete collection of anihpj Django ControllerRevisions to perform bulk cleanup of outdated revision history across services.

    # Delete all old ControllerRevisions for anihpj services
kubectl delete controllerrevisions -n anihpj-services -l version=old

# Delete ControllerRevisions older than specific date
kubectl delete controllerrevisions -n anihpj-services -l created-before=2024-09-01

    Delete collection of anihpj ControllerRevisions after platform-wide archival to external storage for compliance and operational efficiency.

    DaemonSet

    DaemonSet Overview

    DaemonSetSpec - Desired state specification
    DaemonSetStatus - Current observed status
    DaemonSetList - Collection of daemon sets
    Operations - API operations for management
    Official Docs: DaemonSet v1 API | API Version: apps/v1

    DaemonSet represents the configuration of a daemon set that ensures a copy of a pod runs on every node in the cluster or a subset of nodes.

    Description

    DaemonSet represents the configuration of a daemon set. DaemonSets ensure that all (or some) nodes run a copy of a pod. As nodes are added to the cluster, pods are added to them. As nodes are removed from the cluster, those pods are garbage collected. Deleting a DaemonSet will clean up the pods it created. Common uses of DaemonSets include running a cluster storage daemon like glusterd or ceph, running a logs collection daemon like fluentd or logstash, and running a node monitoring daemon like Prometheus Node Exporter.

    Syntax

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: daemonset-name
  namespace: namespace-name
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: daemon-app
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: daemon-app
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: container-name
        image: container-image:tag

    Parameters

    apiVersion (string): API version, always "apps/v1"
    kind (string): Resource type, always "DaemonSet"
    metadata (ObjectMeta): Standard object metadata containing name, namespace, labels, and annotations
    spec (DaemonSetSpec): The desired behavior of this daemon set including pod template and update strategy
    status (DaemonSetStatus): The current status of this daemon set. This data may be out of date by some window of time. Populated by the system. Read-only.

    Return Value

    Returns a DaemonSet object representing the configuration and status of a daemon set that ensures pods run on every matching node.

    Examples

    Example 1: Skills Service Logging DaemonSet

    Create anihpj Skills service logging DaemonSet to collect application logs from all worker nodes running Skills microservice containers.

    # Create Skills logging DaemonSet
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-logger
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-skills-logger
    service: skills
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-skills-logger
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-skills-logger
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: fluentd
        image: fluentd:latest
        env:
        - name: SERVICE_NAME
          value: "anihpj-skills"
EOF

# Get DaemonSet details
kubectl get daemonset anihpj-skills-logger -n anihpj-services
    daemonset.apps/anihpj-skills-logger created NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE NODE SELECTOR AGE anihpj-skills-logger 3 3 3 3 3 10s
    Example 2: Author Service Monitoring DaemonSet

    Deploy anihpj Author service monitoring DaemonSet to collect Elasticsearch metrics and performance data from all nodes hosting Author microservice.

    # Create Author monitoring DaemonSet
kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-author-monitor
  namespace: anihpj-services
  labels:
    app: anihpj-author-monitor
    component: monitoring
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-author-monitor
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-author-monitor
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: node-exporter
        image: prom/node-exporter:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 9100
        env:
        - name: ELASTICSEARCH_SERVICE
          value: "anihpj-author-elasticsearch"
EOF
    daemonset.apps/anihpj-author-monitor created
    Example 3: Location Service Network DaemonSet

    Deploy anihpj Location service network DaemonSet to manage geographic data routing and proximity-based load balancing across cluster nodes.

    # Create Location network DaemonSet
kubectl create daemonset anihpj-location-network \
  --image=nginx:alpine \

    DaemonSetSpec

    DaemonSetSpec is the specification of a daemon set that defines the desired behavior and pod template.

    Description

    DaemonSetSpec is the specification of a daemon set. It defines the desired behavior of the daemon set including pod template, selector requirements, update strategy, and rollback configuration. The spec ensures that the desired number of pods run on matching nodes.

    Syntax

    spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: daemon-app
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: daemon-app
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: container-name
        image: container-image:tag
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
  minReadySeconds: 0
  revisionHistoryLimit: 10

    Parameters

    selector (LabelSelector, required): A label query over pods that are managed by the daemon set. Must match the pod template's labels.
    template (PodTemplateSpec, required): An object that describes the pod that will be created. The DaemonSet will create exactly one copy of this pod on every matching node.
    updateStrategy (DaemonSetUpdateStrategy): An update strategy to replace existing DaemonSet pods with new pods. Can be "RollingUpdate" or "OnDelete".
    minReadySeconds (int32): The minimum number of seconds for which a newly created DaemonSet pod should be ready without crashing.
    revisionHistoryLimit (int32): The number of old history to retain to allow rollback. Defaults to 10.

    Return Value

    Returns a DaemonSetSpec object defining the desired behavior and configuration for daemon set pod deployment across cluster nodes.

    Examples

    Example 1: Skills Service Log Collection Spec

    Configure anihpj Skills service DaemonSetSpec for log collection with rolling update strategy and node selection criteria.

    # Create Skills DaemonSet with specific spec configuration
kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-logs
  namespace: anihpj-services
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-skills-logs
      component: logging
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-skills-logs
        component: logging
    spec:
      nodeSelector:
        service: skills
      containers:
      - name: log-collector
        image: fluentd:v1.14
        resources:
          limits:
            memory: "200Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
  minReadySeconds: 10
EOF
    daemonset.apps/anihpj-skills-logs created
    Example 2: Author Service Elasticsearch Monitoring Spec

    Define anihpj Author service DaemonSetSpec for Elasticsearch monitoring with advanced update strategy and resource constraints.

    # Get existing DaemonSet spec
kubectl get daemonset anihpj-author-monitor -n anihpj-services -o yaml | grep -A 20 "spec:"

# Update DaemonSet spec with enhanced configuration
kubectl patch daemonset anihpj-author-monitor -n anihpj-services --type='merge' -p='{"spec":{"updateStrategy":{"type":"RollingUpdate","rollingUpdate":{"maxUnavailable":"25%"}},"minReadySeconds":15,"revisionHistoryLimit":5}}'
    spec: revisionHistoryLimit: 5 selector: matchLabels: app: anihpj-author-monitor updateStrategy: rollingUpdate: maxUnavailable: 25% type: RollingUpdate daemonset.apps/anihpj-author-monitor patched
    Example 3: Location Service Network Proxy Spec

    Configure anihpj Location service DaemonSetSpec for geographic network proxy with OnDelete update strategy for manual control.

    # Create Location network proxy with OnDelete strategy
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-location-proxy
  namespace: anihpj-services
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-location-proxy
      tier: networking
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-location-proxy
        tier: networking
    spec:
      hostNetwork: true
      containers:
      - name: nginx-proxy
        image: nginx:alpine
        ports:
        - containerPort: 80
          hostPort: 8080
        env:
        - name: UPSTREAM_SERVICE
          value: "anihpj-location-mongodb"
  updateStrategy:
    type: OnDelete
  minReadySeconds: 5
EOF
    daemonset.apps/anihpj-location-proxy created
    Example 4: JobPost Service Analytics Collector Spec

    Define anihpj JobPost service DaemonSetSpec for analytics data collection with resource limits and surge configuration.

    # Create JobPost analytics DaemonSet with surge configuration
kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-collector
  namespace: anihpj-services
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-jobpost-collector
      function: analytics
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost-collector
        function: analytics
    spec:
      tolerations:
      - key: node-role.kubernetes.io/master
        effect: NoSchedule
      containers:
      - name: metrics-collector
        image: prometheus/node-exporter:latest
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "64Mi"
            cpu: "50m"
          limits:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
      maxSurge: 1
EOF
    daemonset.apps/anihpj-jobpost-collector created
    Example 5: Multi-Service Security Agent Spec

    Configure anihpj multi-service DaemonSetSpec for security monitoring with privileged access and comprehensive node coverage.

    # Create security agent DaemonSet with comprehensive spec
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-security-agent
  namespace: anihpj-services
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-security-agent
      security: "true"
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-security-agent
        security: "true"
    spec:
      serviceAccountName: anihpj-security-sa
      hostNetwork: true
      hostPID: true
      containers:
      - name: security-scanner
        image: aquasec/trivy:latest
        securityContext:
          privileged: true
          runAsUser: 0
        volumeMounts:
        - name: docker-socket
          mountPath: /var/run/docker.sock
        env:
        - name: SCAN_SERVICES
          value: "skills,author,location,jobpost"
      volumes:
      - name: docker-socket
        hostPath:
          path: /var/run/docker.sock
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 2
  revisionHistoryLimit: 3
EOF
    daemonset.apps/anihpj-security-agent created

    DaemonSetStatus

    DaemonSetStatus represents the current status of a daemon set including pod distribution and condition information.

    Description

    DaemonSetStatus represents the current status of a daemon set. It provides information about the number of nodes that should be running the daemon pod, how many are currently running, and the overall health of the daemon set deployment across the cluster.

    Syntax

    status:
  currentNumberScheduled: 3
  desiredNumberScheduled: 3
  numberReady: 3
  numberAvailable: 3
  numberUnavailable: 0
  numberMisscheduled: 0
  updatedNumberScheduled: 3
  observedGeneration: 1
  conditions:
  - type: Ready
    status: "True"
    lastTransitionTime: "2024-09-08T10:00:00Z"

    Parameters

    currentNumberScheduled (int32, required): The number of nodes that are running at least 1 daemon pod and are supposed to run the daemon pod.
    desiredNumberScheduled (int32, required): The total number of nodes that should be running the daemon pod.
    numberReady (int32, required): The number of nodes that should be running the daemon pod and have one or more pods running with a Ready condition.
    numberAvailable (int32): The number of nodes that should be running the daemon pod and have one or more pods running and available.
    numberUnavailable (int32): The number of nodes that should be running the daemon pod and have none of the daemon pod running and available.
    numberMisscheduled (int32, required): The number of nodes that are running the daemon pod, but are not supposed to run the daemon pod.
    updatedNumberScheduled (int32): The total number of nodes that are running updated daemon pod.
    conditions ([]DaemonSetCondition): Represents the latest available observations of a DaemonSet's current state.

    Return Value

    Returns a DaemonSetStatus object containing current deployment state, pod distribution metrics, and condition information across cluster nodes.

    Examples

    Example 1: Skills Service DaemonSet Status Monitoring

    Monitor anihpj Skills service DaemonSet status to track log collection pod deployment across worker nodes and identify any scheduling issues.

    # Get Skills DaemonSet status details
kubectl get daemonset anihpj-skills-logs -n anihpj-services -o wide

# Check detailed status information
kubectl describe daemonset anihpj-skills-logs -n anihpj-services | grep -A 10 "Status:"
    NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE NODE SELECTOR AGE anihpj-skills-logs 3 3 3 3 3 service=skills 5m Status: Current Number Scheduled: 3 Desired Number Scheduled: 3 Number Ready: 3 Number Available: 3 Number Unavailable: 0
    Example 2: Author Service Monitoring DaemonSet Health Check

    Examine anihpj Author service monitoring DaemonSet status to verify Elasticsearch metrics collection is functioning across all designated nodes.

    # Get Author monitoring DaemonSet status in JSON format
kubectl get daemonset anihpj-author-monitor -n anihpj-services -o jsonpath='{.status}' | jq .

# Check for any misscheduled or unavailable pods
kubectl get daemonset anihpj-author-monitor -n anihpj-services -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,DESIRED:.status.desiredNumberScheduled,CURRENT:.status.currentNumberScheduled,READY:.status.numberReady,MISSCHEDULED:.status.numberMisscheduled
    { "currentNumberScheduled": 4, "desiredNumberScheduled": 4, "numberAvailable": 4, "numberReady": 4, "numberUnavailable": 0, "numberMisscheduled": 0, "updatedNumberScheduled": 4 }
    Example 3: Location Service Network Proxy Status Analysis

    Analyze anihpj Location service network proxy DaemonSet status to ensure geographic routing is properly distributed across cluster topology.

    # Get Location proxy DaemonSet conditions

    # Get all anihpj DaemonSet status summary

    DaemonSetList

    DaemonSetList is a collection of daemon sets that provides a way to list and manage multiple DaemonSet resources.

    Description

    DaemonSetList is a collection of daemon sets. It provides a way to list and manage multiple DaemonSet resources as a collection, useful for batch operations and comprehensive daemon set management across namespaces.

    Syntax

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSetList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: "string"
items:
  - # Array of DaemonSet objects

    Parameters

    apiVersion (string): API version, always "apps/v1"
    kind (string): Resource type, always "DaemonSetList"
    metadata (ListMeta): Standard list metadata
    items ([]DaemonSet, required): A list of daemon sets

    Return Value

    Returns a DaemonSetList object containing an array of DaemonSet objects matching the specified criteria.

    Examples

    Example 1: Skills Service DaemonSet Collection

    List all anihpj Skills service DaemonSets to review logging and monitoring daemon set deployments for comprehensive service coverage.

    # Get all Skills-related DaemonSets
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-services -l service=skills -o yaml

# List Skills DaemonSets with custom output
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-services -l app=anihpj-skills* -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,READY:.status.numberReady,DESIRED:.status.desiredNumberScheduled
    apiVersion: v1 kind: List items: - apiVersion: apps/v1 kind: DaemonSet metadata: name: anihpj-skills-logs namespace: anihpj-services status: numberReady: 3
    Example 2: Author Service Elasticsearch DaemonSet Inventory

    Retrieve anihpj Author service DaemonSet collection to manage Elasticsearch monitoring and search optimization daemon sets.

    # Get Author service DaemonSet list with labels
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-services -l component=author -o json | jq '.items[] | {name: .metadata.name, ready: .status.numberReady, desired: .status.desiredNumberScheduled}'

# List Author DaemonSets with creation timestamps
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-services -l service=author --sort-by=.metadata.creationTimestamp
    { "name": "anihpj-author-monitor", "ready": 4, "desired": 4 } { "name": "anihpj-author-elasticsearch-exporter", "ready": 4, "desired": 4 }
    Example 3: Location Service Geographic DaemonSet Management

    Manage anihpj Location service DaemonSet collection for geographic data processing and network routing across cluster regions.

    # Get Location service DaemonSets with resource information
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-services -l tier=networking,service=location -o wide

# Export Location DaemonSet collection for backup
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-services -l app=anihpj-location* -o yaml > anihpj-location-daemonsets-backup.yaml
    NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE NODE SELECTOR AGE anihpj-location-proxy 3 3 3 3 3 15m anihpj-location-router 3 3 3 3 3 zone=geo 10m
    Example 4: JobPost Service Analytics DaemonSet Collection

    # Get JobPost analytics DaemonSet collection
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-services -l function=analytics,service=jobpost -o yaml

    DaemonSet Operations

    Overview

    DaemonSet operations provide comprehensive management capabilities for daemon sets in Kubernetes clusters. These operations enable you to create, read, update, delete, and monitor DaemonSets that ensure specific pods run on all (or a subset of) nodes in the cluster.

    DaemonSets are particularly useful for running system-level services, monitoring agents, logging collectors, and other background processes that need to run on every node. The anihpj platform leverages DaemonSets for various background services including skill validation agents, author cache processors, location data indexers, and job post background workers.

    Key Operation Categories
    • Read Operations - Read | Read Status
    • List Operations - List | List All Namespaces
    • Write Operations - Create
    • Update Operations - Update | Update Status
    • Patch Operations - Patch | Patch Status
    • Delete Operations - Delete | Delete Collection
    Common Use Cases
    • System Monitoring - Deploy monitoring agents on every node
    • Log Collection - Run log collection services across all nodes
    • Network Plugins - Install network components on each node
    • Storage Daemons - Deploy storage-related services
    • Security Agents - Run security scanning and monitoring tools
    • Background Processing - Execute background tasks on all nodes
    anihpj Platform Integration

    The anihpj job platform uses DaemonSets for various background services:

    • Skills Service - Skill validation and indexing agents on each node
    • Authors Service - Author data caching and synchronization processors
    • Locations Service - Geographic data processing and mapping services
    • JobPosts Service - Job post indexing and search optimization agents
    • Platform Monitoring - Comprehensive monitoring and alerting systems

    Read DaemonSet

    Read the specified DaemonSet resource to retrieve detailed information about daemon set configuration and current status.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}

    kubectl Syntax

    # Get specific DaemonSet
kubectl get daemonset my-daemonset -n my-namespace

# Get DaemonSet with output formatting
kubectl get daemonset my-daemonset -n my-namespace -o yaml

# Get DaemonSet details
kubectl describe daemonset my-daemonset -n my-namespace

# Get DaemonSet with custom columns
kubectl get daemonset my-daemonset -n my-namespace -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,READY:.status.numberReady

# Get DaemonSet with JSON path
kubectl get daemonset my-daemonset -n my-namespace -o jsonpath='{.status.numberReady}'

    Django Example

    Read anihpj Django DaemonSet to examine daemon set configuration and monitor pod distribution across cluster nodes.

    # Get Skills logging DaemonSet details
kubectl get daemonset anihpj-skills-logs -n anihpj-services

# Get Author monitoring DaemonSet configuration
kubectl describe daemonset anihpj-author-monitor -n anihpj-services
    NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE NODE SELECTOR AGE anihpj-skills-logs 3 3 3 3 3 service=skills 10m
    Example 2: Author Service Elasticsearch Monitoring DaemonSet

# Extract specific DaemonSet configuration

    Read DaemonSet Status

    Read status of the specified DaemonSet resource to retrieve current deployment state and pod distribution information.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}/status

    kubectl Syntax

    # Get DaemonSet status
kubectl get daemonset my-daemonset -n my-namespace -o jsonpath='{.status}'

# Check DaemonSet rollout status
kubectl rollout status daemonset/my-daemonset -n my-namespace

# Get DaemonSet conditions
kubectl get daemonset my-daemonset -n my-namespace -o jsonpath='{.status.conditions}'

# Monitor DaemonSet ready status
kubectl get daemonset my-daemonset -n my-namespace -o custom-columns=READY:.status.numberReady,DESIRED:.status.desiredNumberScheduled

# Watch DaemonSet status changes
kubectl get daemonset my-daemonset -n my-namespace -w

    Django Example

    Read anihpj Django DaemonSet status to monitor daemon set health and track pod deployment progress across cluster nodes.

    # Get Skills DaemonSet status

# Check Author DaemonSet readiness

    List DaemonSet

    List or watch objects of kind DaemonSet.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets

    Path Parameters
    • namespace string, required: object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
    Query Parameters
    • allowWatchBookmarks boolean: allowWatchBookmarks requests watch events with type "BOOKMARK"
    • continue string: continue option should be set when retrieving more results from the server
    • fieldSelector string: selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields
    • labelSelector string: selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels
    • limit integer: limit is a maximum number of responses to return for a list call
    • resourceVersion string: resourceVersion sets a constraint on what resource versions a request may be served from
    • resourceVersionMatch string: resourceVersionMatch determines how resourceVersion is applied to list calls
    • sendInitialEvents boolean: sendInitialEvents controls whether the server will send the events for a watch before sending the current list state
    • timeoutSeconds integer: timeout for the list/watch call
    • watch boolean: watch for changes to the described resources and return them as a stream of add, update, and remove notifications
    Response

    200 (DaemonSetList): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    kubectl syntax
    kubectl get daemonsets
    Example 1: List Skills Service DaemonSets

    List all DaemonSets in the anihpj skills service namespace to monitor background skill validation agents.

    # List all DaemonSets in skills namespace
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-skills

# List DaemonSets with labels
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-skills -l app=skill-validator

# List with custom output format
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-skills -o wide
    NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE NODE SELECTOR AGE skill-validator 3 3 3 3 3 5d skill-indexer 3 3 3 3 3 5d
    Example 2: List Author Service DaemonSets with Field Selector

    List DaemonSets in the anihpj author service using field selectors to filter by metadata fields.

    # List DaemonSets with field selector
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-authors --field-selector metadata.name=author-cache-agent

# List DaemonSets created after specific time
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-authors --field-selector 'metadata.creationTimestamp>2024-01-01T00:00:00Z'

# Combine field and label selectors
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-authors --field-selector metadata.name=author-cache-agent -l component=caching
    NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE NODE SELECTOR AGE author-cache-agent 3 3 3 3 3 3d
    Example 3: List Location Service DaemonSets with Pagination

    List DaemonSets in the anihpj location service using pagination to handle large result sets efficiently.

    # List with limit and continue token
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-locations --limit=10

# Get next page using continue token
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-locations --limit=10 --continue=eyJyZXNvdXJjZVZlcnNpb24...

# Check total count without retrieving all items
kubectl get daemonsets -n anihpj-locations --dry-run=server
    NAME DESIRED CURRENT READY UP-TO-DATE AVAILABLE NODE SELECTOR AGE location-geo-processor 3 3 3 3 3 2d location-mapper 3 3 3 3 3 2d
    Example 4: List JobPost Service DaemonSets with Watch

    Watch DaemonSets in the anihpj jobpost service for real-time monitoring of background job processing agents.

    List DaemonSet for All Namespaces

    List or watch objects of kind DaemonSet across all namespaces.

    HTTP Request

    GET /apis/apps/v1/daemonsets

    Query Parameters
    • allowWatchBookmarks boolean: allowWatchBookmarks requests watch events with type "BOOKMARK"
    • continue string: continue option should be set when retrieving more results from the server
    • fieldSelector string: selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields
    • labelSelector string: selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels
    • limit integer: limit is a maximum number of responses to return for a list call
    • resourceVersion string: resourceVersion sets a constraint on what resource versions a request may be served from
    • resourceVersionMatch string: resourceVersionMatch determines how resourceVersion is applied to list calls
    • sendInitialEvents boolean: sendInitialEvents controls whether the server will send the events for a watch before sending the current list state
    • timeoutSeconds integer: timeout for the list/watch call
    • watch boolean: watch for changes to the described resources and return them as a stream of add, update, and remove notifications
    Response

    200 (DaemonSetList): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    kubectl syntax
    kubectl get daemonsets --all-namespaces

    Create DaemonSet

    Create a DaemonSet.

    HTTP Request

    POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets

    Path Parameters
    • namespace string, required: object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
    Query Parameters
    • dryRun string: when present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
    • fieldManager string: fieldManager is a name associated with the actor or entity that is making these changes
    • fieldValidation string: fieldValidation instructs the server on how to handle objects in the request containing unknown or duplicate fields
    Body Parameters
    • body DaemonSet, required: DaemonSet object to create
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    201 (DaemonSet): Created

    202 (DaemonSet): Accepted

    401: Unauthorized

    kubectl syntax
    kubectl create -f FILENAME
    Example 1: Create Skills Service Validation DaemonSet

    Create a DaemonSet to run skill validation agents on every node in the anihpj skills service cluster.

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: skill-validator
  namespace: anihpj-skills
  labels:
    app: skill-validator
    component: validation
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      name: skill-validator
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        name: skill-validator
        app: skill-validator
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: validator
        image: anihpj/skill-validator:v2.1
        resources:
          limits:
            memory: 200Mi
            cpu: 100m
        env:
        - name: VALIDATION_MODE
          value: "realtime"
        - name: SKILLS_API_ENDPOINT
          value: "http://skills-api:8080"
    daemonset.apps/skill-validator created
    Example 2: Create Author Cache DaemonSet with Node Selector

    Create a DaemonSet for author data caching that runs only on specific nodes in the anihpj authors service.

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: author-cache-agent
  namespace: anihpj-authors
  labels:
    app: author-cache
    tier: caching
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      name: author-cache-agent
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        name: author-cache-agent
        app: author-cache
    spec:
      nodeSelector:
        cache-node: "true"
      containers:
      - name: cache-agent
        image: anihpj/author-cache:v1.5
        ports:
        - containerPort: 6379
        resources:
          limits:
            memory: 512Mi
            cpu: 200m
        env:
        - name: CACHE_SIZE
          value: "256mb"
        - name: AUTHORS_DB_HOST
          value: "authors-db:5432"
    daemonset.apps/author-cache-agent created
    Example 3: Create Location Processing DaemonSet with Volume Mounts

    Create a DaemonSet for location data processing with persistent storage in the anihpj locations service.

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: location-processor
  namespace: anihpj-locations
  labels:
    app: location-processor
    component: data-processing
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      name: location-processor
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        name: location-processor
        app: location-processor
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: processor
        image: anihpj/location-processor:v3.0
        volumeMounts:
        - name: location-data
          mountPath: /data/locations
        - name: geo-cache
          mountPath: /cache/geo
        resources:
          limits:
            memory: 1Gi
            cpu: 500m
        env:
        - name: GEO_API_KEY
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: geo-secrets
              key: api-key
      volumes:
      - name: location-data
        hostPath:
          path: /var/lib/anihpj/locations
      - name: geo-cache
        emptyDir: {}
    daemonset.apps/location-processor created
    Example 4: Create JobPost Indexing DaemonSet with Rolling Update

    Create a DaemonSet for job post indexing with rolling update strategy in the anihpj jobposts service.

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: jobpost-indexer
  namespace: anihpj-jobposts
  labels:
    app: jobpost-indexer
    component: search-indexing
spec:
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      name: jobpost-indexer
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        name: jobpost-indexer
        app: jobpost-indexer
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: indexer
        image: anihpj/jobpost-indexer:v2.3
        resources:
          limits:
            memory: 800Mi
            cpu: 300m
        env:
        - name: ELASTICSEARCH_URL
          value: "http://elasticsearch:9200"
        - name: INDEX_BATCH_SIZE
          value: "100"
        - name: JOBPOSTS_API_ENDPOINT
          value: "http://jobposts-api:8080"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health
            port: 8080
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
    daemonset.apps/jobpost-indexer created
    Example 5: Create Monitoring DaemonSet with Security Context

    Create a DaemonSet for platform monitoring with enhanced security context across anihpj services.

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-monitor
  namespace: anihpj-system
  labels:
    app: platform-monitor
    component: monitoring
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      name: anihpj-monitor
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        name: anihpj-monitor
        app: platform-monitor
    spec:
      serviceAccountName: monitoring-service-account
      securityContext:
        runAsNonRoot: true
        runAsUser: 1000
        fsGroup: 2000
      containers:
      - name: monitor
        image: anihpj/platform-monitor:v4.0
        securityContext:
          allowPrivilegeEscalation: false
          readOnlyRootFilesystem: true
          capabilities:
            drop:
            - ALL
        resources:
          limits:
            memory: 256Mi
            cpu: 150m
        env:
        - name: MONITOR_INTERVAL
          value: "30s"
        - name: SERVICES_LIST
          value: "skills,authors,locations,jobposts"
    daemonset.apps/anihpj-monitor created

    Update DaemonSet

    Replace the specified DaemonSet.

    HTTP Request

    PUT /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}

    Path Parameters
    • name string, required: name of the DaemonSet
    • namespace string, required: object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
    Query Parameters
    • dryRun string: when present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
    • fieldManager string: fieldManager is a name associated with the actor or entity that is making these changes
    • fieldValidation string: fieldValidation instructs the server on how to handle objects in the request containing unknown or duplicate fields
    Body Parameters
    • body DaemonSet, required: Updated DaemonSet object
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    201 (DaemonSet): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    kubectl syntax
    kubectl replace -f FILENAME

    Example 2: Update Author Cache DaemonSet Resources

    Update resource limits and requests for the author cache DaemonSet in anihpj authors service.

    apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: author-cache-agent
  namespace: anihpj-authors
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      name: author-cache-agent
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        name: author-cache-agent
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: cache-agent
        image: anihpj/author-cache:v1.5
        resources:
          limits:
            memory: 1Gi
            cpu: 400m
          requests:
            memory: 512Mi
            cpu: 200m
    daemonset.apps/author-cache-agent replaced

    Patch DaemonSet

    Partially update the specified DaemonSet.

    HTTP Request

    PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}

    Path Parameters
    • name string, required: name of the DaemonSet
    • namespace string, required: object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
    Query Parameters
    • dryRun string: when present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
    • fieldManager string: fieldManager is a name associated with the actor or entity that is making these changes
    • fieldValidation string: fieldValidation instructs the server on how to handle objects in the request containing unknown or duplicate fields
    • force boolean: force is going to "force" Apply requests
    Body Parameters
    • body Patch, required: Patch data for the DaemonSet
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    201 (DaemonSet): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    kubectl syntax
    kubectl patch daemonset NAME --type PATCH_TYPE -p PATCH
    Example 1: Patch Skills Service DaemonSet Image

    Patch the skill validator DaemonSet in anihpj skills service to update the container image version.

    # Patch container image
kubectl patch daemonset skill-validator -n anihpj-skills -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"validator","image":"anihpj/skill-validator:v2.3"}]}}}}'

# Patch using strategic merge
kubectl patch daemonset skill-validator -n anihpj-skills --type='merge' -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"validator","image":"anihpj/skill-validator:v2.3"}]}}}}'

# Patch from file
kubectl patch daemonset skill-validator -n anihpj-skills --patch-file=skill-validator-patch.yaml
    daemonset.apps/skill-validator patched
    Example 2: Patch Author Cache DaemonSet Resources

    Patch the author cache DaemonSet in anihpj authors service to adjust resource limits and requests.

    # Patch memory limits
kubectl patch daemonset author-cache-agent -n anihpj-authors -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"cache-agent","resources":{"limits":{"memory":"2Gi"}}}]}}}}'

# Patch CPU requests
kubectl patch daemonset author-cache-agent -n anihpj-authors -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"cache-agent","resources":{"requests":{"cpu":"300m"}}}]}}}}'

# JSON patch for multiple resource changes
kubectl patch daemonset author-cache-agent -n anihpj-authors --type='json' -p='[{"op": "replace", "path": "/spec/template/spec/containers/0/resources/limits/memory", "value": "2Gi"}]'
    daemonset.apps/author-cache-agent patched daemonset.apps/author-cache-agent patched daemonset.apps/author-cache-agent patched
    Example 3: Patch Location Processing DaemonSet Environment Variables

    Patch the location processor DaemonSet in anihpj locations service to add new environment variables.

    # Add new environment variable

# Patch multiple environment variables

# Remove environment variable using JSON patch

    daemonset.apps/location-processor patched daemonset.apps/location-processor patched daemonset.apps/location-processor patched

    Delete DaemonSet

    Delete a DaemonSet.

    HTTP Request

    DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}

    Path Parameters
    • name string, required: name of the DaemonSet
    • namespace string, required: object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
    Query Parameters
    • dryRun string: when present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
    • gracePeriodSeconds integer: the duration in seconds before the object should be deleted
    • orphanDependents boolean: deprecated: please use the PropagationPolicy
    • propagationPolicy string: whether and how garbage collection will be performed
    Body Parameters
    • body DeleteOptions: delete options for the DaemonSet
    Response

    200 (Status): OK

    202 (Status): Accepted

    401: Unauthorized

    kubectl syntax
    kubectl delete daemonset NAME
    Example 1: Delete Skills Service DaemonSet

    Delete the skill validator DaemonSet from anihpj skills service when no longer needed.

    # Delete DaemonSet immediately
kubectl delete daemonset skill-validator -n anihpj-skills

# Delete with confirmation
kubectl delete daemonset skill-validator -n anihpj-skills --wait=true

# Delete using file
kubectl delete -f skill-validator.yaml
    daemonset.apps "skill-validator" deleted
    Example 2: Delete Author Cache DaemonSet with Grace Period

    Delete the author cache DaemonSet from anihpj authors service with a specified grace period for clean shutdown.

    # Delete with grace period
kubectl delete daemonset author-cache-agent -n anihpj-authors --grace-period=60

# Delete immediately (grace period 0)
kubectl delete daemonset author-cache-agent -n anihpj-authors --grace-period=0 --force

# Delete with cascade policy
kubectl delete daemonset author-cache-agent -n anihpj-authors --cascade=foreground
    daemonset.apps "author-cache-agent" deleted
    Example 3: Delete Location Processing DaemonSet with Dry Run

    Delete the location processor DaemonSet from anihpj locations service using dry run to verify before actual deletion.

    # Dry run delete to check what would be deleted
kubectl delete daemonset location-processor -n anihpj-locations --dry-run=client

# Server dry run
kubectl delete daemonset location-processor -n anihpj-locations --dry-run=server

# Actual delete after verification
kubectl delete daemonset location-processor -n anihpj-locations
    daemonset.apps "location-processor" deleted (dry run) daemonset.apps "location-processor" deleted (server dry run) daemonset.apps "location-processor" deleted
    Example 4: Delete JobPost DaemonSet with Label Selector

    Delete jobpost indexer DaemonSet from anihpj jobposts service using label selectors for targeted deletion.

    # Delete by label selector
kubectl delete daemonset -l app=jobpost-indexer -n anihpj-jobposts

# Delete by multiple labels
kubectl delete daemonset -l app=jobpost-indexer,version=v2.4 -n anihpj-jobposts

# Delete all DaemonSets in namespace
kubectl delete daemonset --all -n anihpj-jobposts
    daemonset.apps "jobpost-indexer" deleted
    Example 5: Delete Monitoring DaemonSet with Background Propagation

    Delete the anihpj platform monitoring DaemonSet using background propagation policy for efficient cleanup.

    # Delete with background propagation
kubectl delete daemonset anihpj-monitor -n anihpj-system --cascade=background

# Delete with orphan propagation (keep pods)
kubectl delete daemonset anihpj-monitor -n anihpj-system --cascade=orphan

# Delete with timeout
kubectl delete daemonset anihpj-monitor -n anihpj-system --timeout=30s
    daemonset.apps "anihpj-monitor" deleted

    Delete Collection of DaemonSets

    Delete collection of DaemonSet.

    HTTP Request

    DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets

    Path Parameters
    • namespace string, required: object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
    Query Parameters
    • continue string: continue option should be set when retrieving more results from the server
    • dryRun string: when present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
    • fieldSelector string: selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields
    • gracePeriodSeconds integer: the duration in seconds before the object should be deleted
    • labelSelector string: selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels
    • limit integer: limit is a maximum number of responses to return for a list call
    • orphanDependents boolean: deprecated: please use the PropagationPolicy
    • propagationPolicy string: whether and how garbage collection will be performed
    • resourceVersion string: resourceVersion sets a constraint on what resource versions a request may be served from
    • resourceVersionMatch string: resourceVersionMatch determines how resourceVersion is applied to list calls
    • sendInitialEvents boolean: sendInitialEvents controls whether the server will send the events for a watch before sending the current list state
    • timeoutSeconds integer: timeout for the list/watch call
    Body Parameters
    • body DeleteOptions: delete options for the collection
    Response

    200 (Status): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    kubectl syntax
    kubectl delete daemonsets --all
    Example 1: Delete All Skills Service DaemonSets

    Delete all DaemonSets in the anihpj skills service namespace for complete cleanup.

    # Delete all DaemonSets in namespace
kubectl delete daemonsets --all -n anihpj-skills

# Delete with confirmation and wait
kubectl delete daemonsets --all -n anihpj-skills --wait=true

# Dry run to check what would be deleted
kubectl delete daemonsets --all -n anihpj-skills --dry-run=client
    daemonset.apps "skill-validator" deleted daemonset.apps "skill-indexer" deleted daemonset.apps "skill-cache" deleted
    Example 2: Delete Author Service DaemonSets by Label

    Delete multiple DaemonSets in the anihpj authors service using label selectors for targeted bulk deletion.

    # Delete by single label
kubectl delete daemonsets -l app=author-service -n anihpj-authors

# Delete by multiple labels
kubectl delete daemonsets -l tier=caching,environment=development -n anihpj-authors

# Delete excluding specific labels
kubectl delete daemonsets -l '!critical' -n anihpj-authors
    daemonset.apps "author-cache-agent" deleted daemonset.apps "author-indexer" deleted
    Example 3: Delete Location Service DaemonSets with Field Selector

    Delete DaemonSets in the anihpj locations service using field selectors for specific criteria-based deletion.

    # Delete by field selector
kubectl delete daemonsets --field-selector metadata.name=location-old-processor -n anihpj-locations

# Delete by creation time
kubectl delete daemonsets --field-selector 'metadata.creationTimestamp<2024-01-01T00:00:00Z' -n anihpj-locations

# Combine field and label selectors
kubectl delete daemonsets -l version=old --field-selector 'metadata.creationTimestamp<2024-01-01T00:00:00Z' -n anihpj-locations
    daemonset.apps "location-old-processor" deleted daemonset.apps "location-legacy-indexer" deleted
    Example 4: Delete JobPost Service DaemonSets with Grace Period

    Delete multiple DaemonSets in the anihpj jobposts service with specified grace period for controlled shutdown.

    # Delete with grace period
kubectl delete daemonsets --all -n anihpj-jobposts --grace-period=120

# Delete immediately with force
kubectl delete daemonsets --all -n anihpj-jobposts --grace-period=0 --force

# Delete with specific propagation policy
kubectl delete daemonsets -l component=processing -n anihpj-jobposts --cascade=foreground
    daemonset.apps "jobpost-processor" deleted daemonset.apps "jobpost-indexer" deleted daemonset.apps "jobpost-cache" deleted
    Example 5: Delete System DaemonSets with Comprehensive Options

    Delete multiple DaemonSets in the anihpj system namespace using comprehensive deletion options for cleanup operations.

    # Delete with timeout and background cascade
kubectl delete daemonsets -l type=monitoring -n anihpj-system --timeout=60s --cascade=background

# Delete with limit and continue
kubectl delete daemonsets --all -n anihpj-system --limit=5

# Delete with dry run and output format
kubectl delete daemonsets --all -n anihpj-system --dry-run=server -o yaml
    daemonset.apps "anihpj-monitor" deleted daemonset.apps "log-collector" deleted daemonset.apps "metrics-agent" deleted
